'' '

Outside , the dawn come greyly in on wing of storm ; Captain Josiah , true to his word , run up the Union Jack at the Four Winds Light and it stream on the fierce wind against the clouded sky like a gallant unquenchable beacon .
CHAPTER V `` THE SOUND OF A GOING '' Rilla run down through the sunlit glory of the maple grove behind Ingleside , to her favourite nook in Rainbow Valley .
She sit down on a green-mossed stone among the fern , prop her chin on her hand and star unseeingly at the dazzle blue sky of the August afternoon -- so blue , so peaceful , so unchanged , just a it have arch over the valley in the mellow day of late summer ever since she could remember .
She want to be alone -- to think thing out -- to adjust herself , if it be possible , to the new world into which she seem to have be transplant with a suddenness and completeness that leave her half bewilder a to her own identity .
Was she -- could she be -- the same Rilla Blythe who have dance at Four Winds Light six day ago -- only six day ago ?
It seem to Rilla that she have live as much in those six day a in all her previous life -- and if it be true that we should count time by heart-throbs she have .
That evening , with it hope and fear and triumph and humiliation , seem like ancient history now .
Could she really ever have cry just because she have be forget and have to walk home with Mary Vance ?
Ah , think Rilla sadly , how trivial and absurd such a cause of tear now appear to her .
She could cry now with a right good will -- but she would not -- she must not .
What be it mother have say , look , with her white lip and stricken eye , a Rilla have never see her mother look before , `` When our woman fail in courage , Shall our men be fearless still ? ''
Yes , that be it .
She must be brave -- like mother -- and Nan -- and Faith -- Faith , who have cry with flashing eye , `` Oh , if I be only a man , to go too ! ''
Only , when her eye ached and her throat burn like this she have to hide herself in Rainbow Valley for a little , just to think thing out and remember that she be n't a child any long -- she be grown-up and woman have to face thing like this .
But it be -- nice -- to get away alone now and then , where nobody could see her and where she need n't feel that people think her a little coward if some tear come in spite of her .
How sweet and woodsey the fern smell !
How softly the great feathery bough of the fir wave and murmur over her !
How elfinly ring the bell of the `` Tree Lovers '' -- just a tinkle now and then a the breeze sweep by !
How purple and elusive the haze where incense be be offer on many an altar of the hill !
How the maple leave whiten in the wind until the grove seem cover with pale silvery blossom !
Everything be just the same a she have see it hundreds of time ; and yet the whole face of the world seem change .
`` How wicked I be to wish that something dramatic would happen ! ''
she think .
`` Oh , if we could only have those dear , monotonous , pleasant day back again !
I would never , never grumble about them again . ''
Rilla 's world have tumble to piece the very day after the party .
As they linger around the dinner table at Ingleside , talk of the war , the telephone have rung .

That be wilful waste , hens to the contrary notwithstanding .
Jem turn to the phone again .
`` I must ring the manse .

a if a knife have be thrust into her , and rush from the room .
Di follow her .

`` I wish you would wake me up .

It make me feel rebellious .
Why should n't thing be the same again -- when everything be over and Jem and Jerry be back ?
We 'll all be happy and jolly again and these day will seem just like a bad dream .
`` The come of the mail be the most exciting event of every day now .
Father just snatch the paper -- I never saw father snatch before -- and the rest of u crowd round and look at the headline over his shoulder .
Susan vow she do not and will not believe a word the paper say but she always come to the kitchen door , and listens and then go back , shake her head .

But then Shirley be the only one of u she never scold .

-LRB- She be the most honest person I know .
She never pretend anything . -RRB-

Oh , I 'm so proud of him !
`` I suppose Kenneth would enlist too if it be n't for his ankle .

He be his mother 's only son and how dreadful she would feel if he go .
Only son should never think of go ! ''
Walter come wander through the valley a Rilla sit there , with his head bent and his hand clasp behind him .

`` Rilla-my-Rilla , what be you think of ? ''

`` Even you -- you 're change .
A week ago we be all so happy -- and -- and -- now I just ca n't find myself at all .
I 'm lose . ''

`` I 'm afraid our old world have come to an end , Rilla .
We 've get to face that fact . ''

`` Sometimes I forget for a little while what it really mean and feel excited and proud -- and then it come over me again like a cold wind . ''
`` I envy Jem ! ''
say Walter moodily .
`` Envy Jem !
Oh , Walter you -- you do n't want to go too . ''
`` No , '' say Walter , gaze straight before him down the emerald vista of the valley , `` no , I do n't want to go .
That 's just the trouble .
Rilla , I 'm afraid to go .
I 'm a coward . ''
`` You 're not ! ''
Rilla burst out angrily .
`` Why , anybody would be afraid to go .
You might be -- why , you might be kill . ''

`` I do n't think I 'm afraid of death itself -- it 's of the pain that might come before death -- it would n't be so bad to die and have it over -- but to keep on die !
Rilla , I 've always be afraid of pain -- you know that .
I ca n't help it -- I shudder when I think of the possibility of be mangle or -- or blind .
Rilla , I can not face that thought .
To be blind -- never to see the beauty of the world again -- moonlight on Four Winds -- the star twinkle through the fir-trees -- mist on the gulf .

I 've felt as fit a ever I do this last month .

`` I wish I could believe it .

So they two sit there in the old valley until the even star shone through a pale-grey , gauzy cloud over the maple grove , and a fragrant dewy darkness fill their little sylvan dell .

When they go back to Ingleside they find caller sit on the veranda .

`` I 'd go myself if I be twenty year younger , '' Norman Douglas be shout .
Norman always shout when he be excite .
`` I 'd show the Kaiser a thing or two !

CHAPTER VI SUSAN , RILLA , AND DOG MONDAY MAKE A RESOLUTION The big living-room at Ingleside be snow over with drift of white cotton .

Nan and Di and Rilla be hard at work .

With dry , anguished eye they be pack up Jem 's belonging .
He must leave for Valcartier the next morning .
They have be expect the word but it be none the less dreadful when it come .
Rilla be baste the hem of a sheet for the first time in her life .
When the word have come that Jem must go she have her cry out among the pine in Rainbow Valley and then she have go to her mother .
`` Mother , I want to do something .
I 'm only a girl -- I ca n't do anything to win the war -- but I must do something to help at home . ''

`` You can help Nan and Di make them up .

`` But , mother -- I 've never do anything like that . ''
`` We will all have to do a great many thing in the month ahead of u that we have never do before , Rilla . ''
`` Well '' -- Rilla take the plunge -- `` I 'll try , mother -- if you 'll tell me how to begin .
I have be think it all over and I have decide that I must be a brave and heroic and unselfish a I can possibly be . ''

Perhaps she do not feel like smile or perhaps she detect a real grain of serious purpose behind Rilla 's romantic pose .
So here be Rilla hem sheet and organize a Junior Red Cross in her thought a she hem ; moreover , she be enjoy it -- the organizing that be , not the hemming .
It be interest and Rilla discover a certain aptitude in herself for it that surprise her .
Who would be president ?
Not she .
The old girl would not like that .
Irene Howard ?
No , somehow Irene be not quite as popular a she deserve to be .
Marjorie Drew ?
No , Marjorie have n't enough backbone .
She be too prone to agree with the last speaker .
Betty Mead -- calm , capable , tactful Betty -- the very one !
And Una Meredith for treasurer ; and , if they be very insistent , they might make her , Rilla , secretary .
As for the various committee , they must be choose after the Juniors be organize , but Rilla know just who should be put on which .
They would meet around -- and there must be no eats -- Rilla know she would have a pitched battle with Olive Kirk over that -- and everything should be strictly business-like and constitutional .
Her minute book should be cover in white with a Red Cross on the cover -- and would n't it be nice to have some kind of uniform which they could all wear at the concert they would have to get up to raise money -- something simple but smart ?
`` You have baste the top hem of that sheet on one side and the bottom hem on the other , '' say Di .

Mrs. Blythe be say upstairs , `` Susan , do you remember that first day Jem lift up his little arm to me and call me ` mo'er ' -- the very first word he ever try to say ? ''

But do not tell me that it will be the final farewell .
He will be back on leave before he go overseas , will he not ? ''
`` We hope so but we be not very sure .
I be make up my mind that he will not , so that there will be no disappointment to bear .

`` I be not go to cry , Mrs. Dr. dear , and that you may tie to , but whether I shall manage to smile or not will be a Providence ordains and a the pit of my stomach feel .

And the shortbread ?
And the mince-pie ?
That bless boy shall not starve , whether they have anything to eat in that Quebec place or not .

Jem Blythe and Jerry Meredith leave next morning .

`` Why ?

-- the train round a curve .

Wherefore , he , Monday , would wait there until the smoking , snort monster , which have carry his hero off , carry him back .
Ay , wait there , little faithful dog with the soft , wistful , puzzled eye .
But it will be many a long bitter day before your boyish comrade come back to you .
The doctor be away on a case that night and Susan stalk into Mrs. Blythe 's room on her way to bed to see if her adored Mrs. Dr. dear be `` comfortable and compose . ''
She pause solemnly at the foot of the bed and solemnly declare , `` Mrs. Dr. dear , I have make up my mind to be a heroine . ''
`` Mrs. Dr. dear '' find herself violently incline to laugh -- which be manifestly unfair , since she have not laugh when Rilla have announce a similar heroic determination .
To be sure , Rilla be a slim , white-robed thing , with a flower-like face and starry young eye aglow with feeling ; whereas Susan be array in a grey flannel nightgown of strait simplicity , and have a strip of red woollen worst tied around her grey hair a a charm against neuralgia .
But that should not make any vital difference .
Was it not the spirit that count ?
Yet Mrs. Blythe be hard put to it not to laugh .
`` I be not , '' proceed Susan firmly , `` go to lament or whine or question the wisdom of the Almighty any more a I have be do lately .
Whining and shirk and blame Providence do not get u anywhere .
We have just get to grapple with whatever we have to do whether it be weed the onion patch , or run the Government .
I shall grapple .
Those bless boy have go to war ; and we woman , Mrs. Dr. dear , must tarry by the stuff and keep a stiff upper lip . ''
CHAPTER VII A WAR-BABY AND A SOUP TUREEN `` Liege and Namur -- and now Brussels ! ''
The doctor shake his head .
`` I do n't like it -- I do n't like it . ''
`` Do not you lose heart , Dr. dear ; they be just defend by foreigner , '' say Susan superbly .
`` Wait you till the Germans come against the British ; there will be a very different story to tell and that you may tie to . ''
The doctor shake his head again , but a little less gravely ; perhaps they all share subconsciously in Susan 's belief that `` the thin grey line '' be unbreakable , even by the victorious rush of Germany 's ready million .
At any rate , when the terrible day come -- the first of many terrible day -- with the news that the British army be drive back they star at each other in blank dismay .
`` It -- it ca n't be true , '' gasp Nan , take a brief refuge in temporary incredulity .
`` I felt that there be to be bad news today , '' say Susan , `` for that cat-creature turn into Mr. Hyde this morning without rhyme or reason for it , and that be no good omen . '' '' '
A broken , a beaten , but not a demoralize , army , ' '' mutter the doctor , from a London dispatch .
`` Can it be England 's army of which such a thing be say ? ''
`` It will be a long time now before the war be end , '' say Mrs. Blythe despairingly .
Susan 's faith , which have for a moment be temporarily submerge , now reappear triumphantly .
`` Remember , Mrs. Dr. dear , that the British army be not the British navy .
Never forget that .
And the Russians be on their way , too , though Russians be people I do not know much about and consequently will not tie to . ''
`` The Russians will not be in time to save Paris , '' say Walter gloomily .
`` Paris be the heart of France -- and the road to it be open .
Oh , I wish '' -- he stop abruptly and go out .
After a paralysed day the Ingleside folk find it be possible to `` carry on '' even in the face of ever-darkening bad news .
Susan work fiercely in her kitchen , the doctor go out on his round of visit , Nan and Di return to their Red Cross activity ; Mrs. Blythe go to Charlottetown to attend a Red Cross Convention ; Rilla after relieve her feeling by a stormy fit of tear in Rainbow Valley and an outburst in her diary , remember that she have elect to be brave and heroic .
And , she think , it really be heroic to volunteer to drive about the Glen and Four Winds one day , collect promise Red Cross supply with Abner Crawford 's old grey horse .
One of the Ingleside horse be lame and the doctor need the other , so there be nothing for it but the Crawford nag , a placid , unhasting , thick-skinned creature with an amiable habit of stop every few yard to kick a fly off one leg with the foot of the other .
Rilla felt that this , couple with the fact that the Germans be only fifty mile from Paris , be hardly to be endure .
But she start off gallantly on an errand fraught with amazing result .
Late in the afternoon she find herself , with a buggy full of parcel , at the entrance to a grassy , deep-rutted lane lead to the harbour shore , wonder whether it be worth while to call down at the Anderson house .
The Andersons be desperately poor and it be not likely Mrs. Anderson have anything to give .
On the other hand , her husband , who be an Englishman by birth and who have be work in Kingsport when the war break out , have promptly sail for England to enlist there , without , it may be say , come home or send much hard cash to represent him .
So possibly Mrs. Anderson might feel hurt if she be overlook .
Rilla decide to call .
There be time afterwards when she wish she have n't , but in the long run she be very thankful that she do .
The Anderson house be a small and tumbledown affair , crouch in a grove of battered spruce near the shore a if rather ashamed of itself and anxious to hide .
Rilla tie her grey nag to the rickety fence and go to the door .
It be open ; and the sight she saw bereft her temporarily of the power of speech or motion .
Through the open door of the small bedroom opposite her , Rilla saw Mrs. Anderson lie on the untidy bed ; and Mrs. Anderson be dead .
There be no doubt of that ; neither be there any doubt that the big , frowzy , red-headed , red-faced , over-fat woman sit near the door-way , smoke a pipe quite comfortably , be very much alive .
She rock idly back and forth amid her surroundings of squalid disorder , and pay no attention whatever to the piercing wail proceed from a cradle in the middle of the room .
Rilla know the woman by sight and reputation .
Her name be Mrs. Conover ; she live down at the fishing village ; she be a great-aunt of Mrs. Anderson ; and she drink as well a smoke .
Rilla 's first impulse be to turn and flee .
But that would never do .
Perhaps this woman , repulsive a she be , need help -- though she certainly do not look a if she be worry over the lack of it .
`` Come in , '' say Mrs. Conover , remove her pipe and staring at Rilla with her little , rat-like eye .
`` Is -- be Mrs. Anderson really dead ? ''
ask Rilla timidly , a she step over the sill .
`` Dead a a door nail , '' respond Mrs. Conover cheerfully .
`` Kicked the bucket half an hour ago .
I 've send Jen Conover to ` phone for the undertaker and get some help up from the shore .
You 're the doctor 's miss , ai n't ye ?
Have a cheer ? ''
Rilla do not see any chair which be not clutter with something .
She remain stand .
`` Was n't it -- very sudden ? ''
`` Well , she 's be a-pining ever since that worthless Jim light out for England -- which I say it 's a pity a he ever leave .
It 's my belief she be take for death when she hear the news .
That young un there be bear a fortnight ago and since then she 's just go down and today she up and die , without a soul expect it . ''
`` Is there anything I can do to -- to help ? ''
hesitate Rilla .
`` Bless yez , no -- unless ye 've a knack with kid .
I have n't .
That young un there never let up squall , day or night .
I 've just get that I take no notice of it . ''
Rilla tiptoe gingerly over to the cradle and more gingerly still pull down the dirty blanket .
She have no intention of touch the baby -- she have no `` knack with kid '' either .
She saw an ugly midget with a red , distort little face , roll up in a piece of dingy old flannel .
She have never see an ugly baby .
Yet a feeling of pity for the desolate , orphan mite which have `` come out of the everywhere '' into such a dubious `` here '' , take sudden possession of her .
`` What be go to become of the baby ? ''
she ask .
`` Lord know , '' say Mrs. Conover candidly .
`` Min worry awful over that before she die .
She keep on a-saying ` Oh , what will become of my pore baby ' till it really get on my nerve .
I ai n't a-going to trouble myself with it , I can tell yez .
I brung up a boy that my sister leave and he skin out as soon a he get to be some good and wo n't give me a mite o ' help in my old age , ungrateful whelp a he be .
I tell Min it 'd have to be send to an orphan asylum till we 'd see if Jim ever come back to look after it .
Would yez believe it , she do n't relish the idee .
But that 's the long and short of it . ''
`` But who will look after it until it can be take to the asylum ? ''
persist Rilla .
Somehow the baby 's fate worry her .
`` S'pose I 'll have to , '' grunt Mrs. Conover .
She put away her pipe and take an unblushing swig from a black bottle she produce from a shelf near her .
`` It 's my opinion the kid wo n't live long .
It 's sickly .
Min never have no gimp and I guess it hai n't either .
Likely it wo n't trouble any one long and good riddance , sez I. '' Rilla draw the blanket down a little farther .
`` Why , the baby be n't dress ! ''
she exclaim , in a shocked tone .
`` Who be to dress him I 'd like to know , '' demand Mrs. Conover truculently .
`` I have n't time -- take me all the time there be look after Min .
` Sides , a I tell yez , I do n't know nithing about kid .
Old Mrs. Billy Crawford , she be here when it be bear and she wash it and roll it up in that flannel , and Jen she 's tend it a bit since .
The critter be warm enough .
This weather would melt a brass monkey . ''

She have never encounter any of the tragedy of life before and this one smote her to the core of her heart .
The thought of the poor mother go down into the valley of the shadow alone , fret about her baby , with no one near but this abominable old woman , hurt her terribly .
If she have only come a little sooner !
Yet what could she have do -- what could she do now ?
She do n't know , but she must do something .
She hat baby -- but she simply could not go away and leave that poor little creature with Mrs. Conover -- who be apply herself again to her black bottle and would probably be helplessly drunk before anybody come .
`` I ca n't stay , '' think Rilla .
`` Mr. Crawford say I must be home by supper-time because he want the pony this evening himself .
Oh , what can I do ? ''
She make a sudden , desperate , impulsive resolution .
`` I 'll take the baby home with me , '' she say .
`` Can I ? ''
`` Sure , if yez want to , '' say Mrs. Conover amiably .
`` I hai n't any objection .
Take it and welcome . ''
`` I -- I ca n't carry it , '' say Rilla .
`` I have to drive the horse and I 'd be afraid I 'd drop it .
Is there a -- a basket anywhere that I could put it in ? ''
`` Not a I know on .
There ai n't much here of anything , I kin tell yez .
Min be pore and as shiftless a Jim .
Ef ye open that drawer over there yez 'll find a few baby clo'es .
Best take them along . ''
Rilla get the clothes -- the cheap , sleazy garment the poor mother have make ready a best she could .
But this do not solve the pressing problem of the baby 's transportation .
Rilla look helplessly round .
Oh , for mother -- or Susan !
Her eye fell on an enormous blue soup tureen at the back of the dresser .
`` May I have this to -- to lay him in ? ''
she ask .
`` Well , ` tai n't mine but I guess yez kin take it .
Do n't smash it if yez can help -- Jim might make a fuss about it if he come back alive -- which he sure will , seein ' he ai n't any good .
He brung that old tureen out from England with him -- say it 'd always be in the family .
Him and Min never use it -- never have enough soup to put in it -- but Jim think the world of it .
He be mighty perticuler about some thing but do n't worry him none that there be n't much in the way o ' eatable to put in the dish . ''
For the first time in her life Rilla Blythe touch a baby -- lift it -- roll it in a blanket , tremble with nervousness l she drop it or -- or -- break it .
Then she put it in the soup tureen .
`` Is there any fear of it smother ? ''
she ask anxiously .
`` Not much odds if it do , '' say Mrs. Conover .
Horrified Rilla loosen the blanket round the baby 's face a little .
The mite have stop cry and be blink up at her .
It have big dark eye in it ugly little face .
`` Better not let the wind blow on it , '' admonish Mrs. Conover .
`` Take it breath if it do . ''
Rilla wrap the tattered little quilt around the soup tureen .
`` Will you hand this to me after I get into the buggy , please ? ''
`` Sure I will , '' say Mrs. Conover , get up with a grunt .
And so it be that Rilla Blythe , who have drive to the Anderson house a self-confessed hater of baby , drive away from it carry one in a soup tureen on her lap !
Rilla think she would never get to Ingleside .
In the soup tureen there be an uncanny silence .
In one way she be thankful the baby do not cry but she wish it would give an occasional squeak to prove that it be alive .
Suppose it be smother !

She be a thankful girl when at last she reach harbour at Ingleside .
Rilla carry the soup tureen to the kitchen , and set it on the table under Susan 's eye .

`` What in the world be this ? ''
ask the doctor , come in .
Rilla pour out her story .

`` What be you go to do with it ? ''
ask the doctor coolly .
Rilla have n't exactly expect this kind of question .

Presently the doctor confront Rilla .
`` A young baby mean a great deal of additional work and trouble in a household , Rilla .
Nan and Di be leave for Redmond next week and neither your mother nor Susan be able to assume so much extra care under present condition .

`` Me ! ''
Rilla be dismay into be ungrammatical .
`` Why -- father -- I -- I could n't ! ''
