My advice and Susan 's be at your disposal .
If you can not , then the baby must go back to Meg Conover .
Its lease of life will be short if it do for it be evident that it be a delicate child and require particular care .
I doubt if it would survive even if send to an orphan ' home .
But I can not have your mother and Susan over-taxed . ''
The doctor walk out of the kitchen , look very stern and immovable .
In his heart he know quite well that the small inhabitant of the big soup tureen would remain at Ingleside , but he mean to see if Rilla could not be induce to rise to the occasion .
Rilla sit look blankly at the baby .
It be absurd to think she could take care of it .
But -- that poor little , frail , dead mother who have worry about it -- that dreadful old Meg Conover .
`` Susan , what must be do for a baby ? ''
she ask dolefully .
`` You must keep it warm and dry and wash it every day , and be sure the water be neither too hot nor too cold , and fee it every two hour .
If it have colic , you put hot thing on it stomach , '' say Susan , rather feebly and flatly for her .
The baby begin to cry again .
`` It must be hungry -- it have to be feed anyhow , '' say Rilla desperately .
`` Tell me what to get for it , Susan , and I 'll get it . ''
Under Susan 's direction a ration of milk and water be prepare , and a bottle obtain from the doctor 's office .
Then Rilla lift the baby out of the soup tureen and feed it .
She bring down the old basket of her own infancy from the attic and lay the now sleep baby in it .
She put the soup tureen away in the pantry .
Then she sit down to think thing over .
The result of her thinking thing over be that she go to Susan when the baby wake .
`` I 'm go to see what I can do , Susan .
I ca n't let that poor little thing go back to Mrs. Conover .
Tell me how to wash and dress it . ''
Under Susan 's supervision Rilla bath the baby .
Susan dare not help , other than by suggestion , for the doctor be in the living-room and might pop in at any moment .
Susan have learn by experience that when Dr. Blythe put his foot down and say a thing must be , that thing be .
Rilla set her teeth and go ahead .
In the name of goodness , how many wrinkle and kink do a baby have ?
Why , there be n't enough of it to take hold of .
Oh , suppose she let it slip into the water -- it be so wobbly !
If it would only stop howl like that !
How could such a tiny morsel make such an enormous noise .
Its shriek could be hear over Ingleside from cellar to attic .
`` Am I really hurt it much , Susan , do you suppose ? ''
she ask piteously .
`` No , dearie .
Most new baby hate like poison to be wash .
You be real knacky for a beginner .
Keep your hand under it back , whatever you do , and keep cool . ''
Keep cool !
Rilla be ooze perspiration at every pore .
When the baby be dry and dress and temporarily quiet with another bottle she be as limp a a rag .
`` What must I do with it tonight , Susan ? ''
A baby by day be dreadful enough ; a baby by night be unthinkable .
`` Set the basket on a chair by your bed and keep it cover .
You will have to fee it once or twice in the night , so you would better take the oil heater upstairs .
If you can not manage it call me and I will go , doctor or no doctor . ''
`` But , Susan , if it cry ? ''
The baby , however , do not cry .
It be surprisingly good -- perhaps because it poor little stomach be fill with proper food .
It sleep most of the night but Rilla do not .
She be afraid to go to sleep for fear something would happen to the baby .
She prepare it three o'clock ration with a grim determination that she would not call Susan .
Oh , be she dream ?
Was it really she , Rilla Blythe , who have get into this absurd predicament ?
She do not care if the Germans be near Paris -- she do not care if they be in Paris -- if only the baby would n't cry or choke or smother or have convulsion .
Babies do have convulsion , do n't they ?
Oh , why have she forget to ask Susan what she must do if the baby have convulsion ?
She reflect rather bitterly that father be very considerate of mother 's and Susan 's health , but what about hers ?
Did he think she could continue to exist if she never get any sleep ?
But she be not go to back down now -- not she .
She would look after this detestable little animal if it kill her .
She would get a book on baby hygiene and be behold to nobody .
She would never go to father for advice -- she would n't bother mother -- and she would only condescend to Susan in dire extremity .
They would all see !
Thus it come about that Mrs. Blythe , when she return home two night later and ask Susan where Rilla be , be electrify by Susan 's composed reply .
`` She 's upstairs , Mrs. Dr. dear , put her baby to bed . ''
CHAPTER VIII RILLA DECIDES Families and individual alike soon become use to new condition and accept them unquestioningly .
By the time a week have elapse it seem a it the Anderson baby have always be at Ingleside .
After the first three distract night Rilla begin to sleep again , wake automatically to attend to her charge on schedule time .
She bath and fed and dress it as skilfully a if she have be do it all her life .
She like neither her job nor the baby any the good ; she still handle it as gingerly a if it be some kind of a small lizard , and a breakable lizard at that ; but she do her work thoroughly and there be not a cleaner , better-cared-for infant in Glen St. Mary .
She even take to weigh the creature every day and jot the result down in her diary ; but sometimes she ask herself pathetically why unkind destiny have ever lead her down the Anderson lane on that fatal day .
Shirley , Nan , and Di do not tease her as much a she have expect .
They all seem rather stun by the mere fact of Rilla adopt a war-baby ; perhaps , too , the doctor have issue instruction .
Walter , of course , never have tease her over anything ; one day he tell her she be a brick .
`` It take more courage for you to tackle that five pound of new infant , Rilla-my-Rilla , than it would be for Jem to face a mile of Germans .
I wish I have half your pluck , '' he say ruefully .
Rilla be very proud of Walter 's approval ; nevertheless , she write gloomily in her diary that night : -- `` I wish I could like the baby a little bit .
It would make thing easy .
But I do n't .
I 've hear people say that when you take care of a baby you get fond of it -- but you do n't -- I do n't , anyway .
And it 's a nuisance -- it interfere with everything .
It just tie me down -- and now of all time when I 'm try to get the Junior Reds start .
And I could n't go to Alice Clow 's party last night and I be just die to .
Of course father be n't really unreasonable and I can always get an hour or two off in the evening when it 's necessary ; but I know he would n't stand for my be out half the night and leave Susan or mother to see to the baby .
I suppose it be just as well , because the thing do take colic -- or something -- about one o'clock .
It do n't kick or stiffen out , so I know that , accord to Morgan , it be n't cry for temper ; and it be n't hungry and no pin be stick in it .
It scream till it be black in the face ; I get up and heated water and put the hot-water bottle on it stomach , and it howl bad than ever and draw up it poor wee thin leg .
I be afraid I have burn it but I do n't believe I do .
Then I walk the floor with it although ` Morgan on Infants ' say that should never be do .
I walk mile , and oh , I be so tired and discouraged and mad -- yes , I be .
I could have shake the creature if it have be big enough to shake , but it be n't .
Father be out on a case , and mother have have a headache and Susan be squiffy because when she and Morgan differ I insist upon go by what Morgan say , so I be determine I would n't call her unless I have to .
`` Finally , Miss Oliver come in .
She have room with Nan now , not me , all because of the baby , and I be broken-hearted about it .
I miss our long talk after we go to bed , so much .
It be the only time I ever have her to myself .
I hat to think the baby 's yell have waken her up , for she have so much to bear now .
Mr. Grant be at Valcartier , too , and Miss Oliver feel it dreadfully , though she be splendid about it .
She think he will never come back and her eye just break my heart -- they be so tragic .
She say it be n't the baby that wake her -- she have n't be able to sleep because the Germans be so near Paris ; she take the little wretch and lay it flat on it stomach across her knee and thump it back gently a few time , and it stop shriek and go right off to sleep and sleep like a lamb the rest of the night .
I do n't -- I be too wear out .
`` I 'm have a perfectly dreadful time get the Junior Reds start .
I succeed in get Betty Mead a president , and I be secretary , but they put Jen Vickers in a treasurer and I despise her .
She be the sort of girl who call any clever , handsome , or distinguish people she know slightly by their first name -- behind their back .
And she be sly and two-faced .
Una do n't mind , of course .
She be willing to do anything that come to hand and never mind whether she have an office or not .
She be just a perfect angel , while I be only angelic in spot and demonic in other spot .
I wish Walter would take a fancy to her , but he never seem to think about her in that way , although I hear him say once she be like a tea rise .
She be too .
And she get impose upon , just because she be so sweet and willing ; but I do n't allow people to impose on Rilla Blythe and ` that you may tie to , ' a Susan say .
`` Just a I expect , Olive be determine we should have lunch serve at our meeting .
We have a battle royal over it .
The majority be against eats and now the minority be sulk .
Irene Howard be on the eats side and she have be very cool to me ever since and it make me feel miserable .
I wonder if mother and Mrs. Elliott have problem in the Senior Society too .
I suppose they have , but they just go on calmly in spite of everything .
I go on -- but not calmly -- I rage and cry -- but I do it all in private and blow off steam in this diary ; and when it 's over I vow I 'll show them .
I never sulk .
I detest people who sulk .
Anyhow , we 've get the society start and we 're to meet once a week , and we 're all go to learn to knit .
`` Shirley and I go down to the station again to try to induce Dog Monday to come home but we fail .
All the family have try and fail .
Three day after Jem have go Walter go down and bring Monday home by main force in the buggy and shut him up for three day .
Then Monday go on a hunger strike and howl like a Banshee night and day .
We have to let him out or he would have starve to death .
`` So we have decide to let him alone and father have arrange with the butcher near the station to fee him with bone and scrap .
Besides , one of u go down nearly every day to take him something .
He just lie curl up in the shipping-shed , and every time a train come in he will rush over to the platform , wag his tail expectantly , and tear around to every one who come off the train .
And then , when the train go and he realize that Jem have not come , he creep dejectedly back to his shed , with his disappointed eye , and lie down patiently to wait for the next train .
Mr. Gray , the station master , say there be time when he can hardly help cry from sheer sympathy .
One day some boy throw stone at Monday and old Johnny Mead , who never be know to take notice of anything before , snatch up a meat axe in the butcher 's shop and chase them through the village .
Nobody have molest Monday since .
`` Kenneth Ford have go back to Toronto .
He come up two evening ago to say good-bye .
I be n't home -- some clothes have to be make for the baby and Mrs. Meredith offer to help me , so I be over at the manse , and I do n't see Kenneth .
Not that it matter ; he tell Nan to say good-bye to Spider for him and tell me not to forget him wholly in my absorb maternal duty .
If he could leave such a frivolous , insulting message a that for me it show plainly that our beautiful hour on the sandshore mean nothing to him and I be not go to think about him or it again .
`` Fred Arnold be at the manse and walk home with me .
He be the new Methodist minister 's son and very nice and clever , and would be quite handsome if it be not for his nose .
It be a really dreadful nose .
When he talk of commonplace thing it do not matter so much , but when he talk of poetry and ideals the contrast between his nose and his conversation be too much for me and I want to shriek with laughter .
It be really not fair , because everything he say be perfectly charm and if somebody like Kenneth have say it I would have be enrapture .
When I listen to him with my eye cast down I be quite fascinate ; but as soon a I look up and saw his nose the spell be break .
He want to enlist , too , but ca n't because he be only seventeen .
Mrs. Elliott meet u a we be walk through the village and could not have look more horrified if she catch me walk with the Kaiser himself .
Mrs. Elliott detest the Methodists and all their work .
Father say it be an obsession with her . ''
About 1st September there be an exodus from Ingleside and the manse .
Faith , Nan , Di and Walter leave for Redmond ; Carl betook himself to his Harbour Head school and Shirley be off to Queen 's .
Rilla be leave alone at Ingleside and would have be very lonely if she have have time to be .
She miss Walter keenly ; since their talk in Rainbow Valley they have grow very near together and Rilla discuss problem with Walter which she never mention to others .
But she be so busy with the Junior Reds and her baby that there be rarely a spare minute for loneliness ; sometimes , after she go to bed , she cry a little in her pillow over Walter 's absence and Jem at Valcartier and Kenneth 's unromantic farewell message , but she be generally asleep before the tear get fairly start .
`` Shall I make arrangement to have the baby send to Hopetown ? ''
the doctor ask one day two week after the baby 's arrival at Ingleside .
For a moment Rilla be tempt to say `` Yes . ''
The baby could be send to Hopetown -- it would be decently look after -- she could have her free day and untrammelled night back again .
But -- but -- that poor young mother who have n't want it to go to the asylum !
Rilla could n't get that out of her thought .
And that very morning she discover that the baby have gain eight ounce since it come to Ingleside .
Rilla have felt such a thrill of pride over this .
`` You -- you say it might n't live if it go to Hopetown , '' she say .
`` It might n't .
Somehow , institutional care , no matter how good it may be , do n't always succeed with delicate baby .
But you know what it mean if you want it keep here , Rilla . ''
`` I 've take care of it for a fortnight -- and it have gain half a pound , '' cry Rilla .
`` I think we 'd better wait until we hear from it father anyhow .
He might n't want to have it send to an orphan asylum , when he be fight the battle of his country . ''
The doctor and Mrs. Blythe exchange amuse , satisfied smile behind Rilla 's back ; and nothing more be say about Hopetown .
Then the smile fade from the doctor 's face ; the Germans be twenty mile from Paris .
Horrible tale be begin to appear in the paper of deed do in martyred Belgium .
Life be very tense at Ingleside for the old people .
`` We eat up the war news , '' Gertrude Oliver tell Mrs. Meredith , try to laugh and fail .
`` We study the map and nip the whole Hun army in a few well-directed strategic move .
But Papa Joffre have n't the benefit of our advice -- and so Paris -- must -- fall . ''
`` Will they reach it -- will not some mighty hand yet intervene ? ''
murmur John Meredith .
`` I teach school like one in a dream , '' continue Gertrude ; `` then I come home and shut myself in my room and walk the floor .
I be wear a path right across Nan 's carpet .
We be so horribly near this war . ''
`` Them German men be at Senlis .
Nothing nor nobody can save Paris now , '' wail Cousin Sophia .
Cousin Sophia have take to read the newspaper and have learn more about the geography of northern France , if not about the pronunciation of French name , in her seventy-first year than she have ever know in her schooldays .
`` I have not such a poor opinion of the Almighty , or of Kitchener , '' say Susan stubbornly .
`` I see there be a Bernstoff man in the States who say that the war be over and Germany have win -- and they tell me Whiskers-on-the-moon say the same thing and be quite pleased about it , but I could tell them both that it be chancy work counting chicken even the day before they be hatch , and bear have be know to live long after their skin be sell . ''
`` Why ai n't the British navy do more ? ''
persist Cousin Sophia .
`` Even the British navy can not sail on dry land , Sophia Crawford .
I have not give up hope , and I shall not , Tomascow and Mobbage and all such barbarous name to the contrary notwithstanding .
Mrs. Dr. dear , can you tell me if R-h-e-i-m-s be Rimes or Reems or Rames or Rems ? ''
`` I believe it 's really more like ` Rhangs , ' Susan . ''
`` Oh , those French name , '' groan Susan .
`` They tell me the Germans have about ruin the church there , '' sigh Cousin Sophia .
`` I always think the Germans be Christians . ''
`` A church be bad enough but their doings in Belgium be far bad , '' say Susan grimly .
`` When I hear the doctor read about them bayonet the baby , Mrs. Dr. dear , I just think , ` Oh , what if it be our little Jem ! '
I be stir the soup when that think come to me and I just felt that if I could have lift that saucepan full of that boil soup and throw it at the Kaiser I would not have live in vain . ''
`` Tomorrow -- tomorrow -- will bring the news that the Germans be in Paris , '' say Gertrude Oliver , through her tense lip .
She have one of those soul that be always tie to the stake , burn in the suffering of the world around them .
Apart from her own personal interest in the war , she be rack by the thought of Paris fall into the ruthless hand of the horde who have burn Louvain and ruin the wonder of Rheims .
But on the morrow and the next morrow come the news of the miracle of the Marne .
Rilla rush madly home from the office wave the Enterprise with it big red headline .
Susan run out with tremble hand to hoist the flag .
The doctor stalk about mutter `` Thank God . ''
Mrs. Blythe cry and laugh and cry again .
`` God just put out His hand and touch them -- ` thus far -- no farther ' , '' say Mr. Meredith that even .
Rilla be sing upstairs a she put the baby to bed .
Paris be save -- the war be over -- Germany have lose -- there would soon be an end now -- Jem and Jerry would be back .
The black cloud have roll by .
`` Do n't you dare have colic this joyful night , '' she tell the baby .
`` If you do I 'll clap you back into your soup tureen and ship you off to Hopetown -- by freight -- on the early train .
You have get beautiful eye -- and you 're not quite a red and wrinkle a you be -- but you have n't a speck of hair -- and your hand be like little claw -- and I do n't like you a bit good than I ever do .
But I hope your poor little white mother know that you 're tuck in a soft basket with a bottle of milk as rich a Morgan allow instead of perish by inch with old Meg Conover .
And I hope she do n't know that I nearly drown you that first morning when Susan be n't there and I let you slip right out of my hand into the water .
Why will you be so slippery ?
No , I do n't like you and I never will but for all that I 'm go to make a decent , upstanding infant of you .
You be go to get as fat a a self-respecting child should be , for one thing .
I be not go to have people say ` what a puny little thing that baby of Rilla Blythe 's be ' a old Mrs. Drew say at the senior Red Cross yesterday .
If I ca n't love you I mean to be proud of you at least . ''
CHAPTER IX DOC HAS A MISADVENTURE `` The war will not be over before next spring now , '' say Dr. Blythe , when it become apparent that the long battle of the Aisne have result in a stalemate .
Rilla be murmur `` knit four , purl one '' under her breath , and rock the baby 's cradle with one foot .
Morgan disapprove of cradle for baby but Susan do not , and it be worth while to make some slight sacrifice of principle to keep Susan in good humour .
She lay down her knitting for a moment and say , `` Oh , how can we bear it so long ? ''
-- then pick up her sock and go on .
The Rilla of two month before would have rush off to Rainbow Valley and cry .
Miss Oliver sigh and Mrs. Blythe clasp her hand for a moment .
Then Susan say briskly , `` Well , we must just gird up our loin and pitch in .
Business a usual be England 's motto , they tell me , Mrs. Dr. dear , and I have take it for mine , not think I could easily find a good .
I shall make the same kind of pudding today I always make on Saturday .
It be a good deal of trouble to make , and that be well , for it will employ my thought .
I will remember that Kitchener be at the helm and Joffer be do very well for a Frenchman .
I shall get that box of cake off to little Jem and finish that pair of sock today likewise .
A sock a day be my allowance .
Old Mrs. Albert Mead of Harbour Head manage a pair and a half a day but she have nothing to do but knit .
You know , Mrs. Dr. dear , she have be bed-rid for year and she have be worry terrible because she be no good to anybody and a dreadful expense , and yet could not die and be out of the way .
And now they tell me she be quite chirk up and resign to live because there be something she can do , and she knit for the soldier from daylight to dark .
Even Cousin Sophia have take to knit , Mrs. Dr. dear , and it be a good thing , for she can not think of quite so many doleful speech to make when her hand be busy with her needle instead of be fold on her stomach .
She think we will all be Germans this time next year but I tell her it will take more than a year to make a German out of me .
Do you know that Rick MacAllister have enlist , Mrs. Dr. dear ?
And they say Joe Milgrave would too , only he be afraid that if he do that Whiskers-on-the-moon will not let him have Miranda .
Whiskers say that he will believe the story of German atrocity when he see them , and that it be a good thing that Rangs Cathedral have be destroy because it be a Roman Catholic church .
Now , I be not a Roman Catholic , Mrs. Dr. dear , be bear and breed a good Presbyterian and meaning to live and die one , but I maintain that the Catholics have as good a right to their church a we have to ours and that the Huns have no kind of business to destroy them .
Just think , Mrs. Dr. dear , '' conclude Susan pathetically , `` how we would feel if a German shell knock down the spire of our church here in the glen , and I 'm sure it be every bit a bad to think of Rangs cathedral be hammer to piece . ''
And , meanwhile , everywhere , the lad of the world rich and poor , low and high , white and brown , be follow the Piper 's call .
`` Even Billy Andrews ' boy be go -- and Jane 's only son -- and Diana 's little Jack , '' say Mrs. Blythe .
`` Priscilla 's son have go from Japan and Stella 's from Vancouver -- and both the Rev . Jo 's boy .
Philippa write that her boy ` go right away , not be afflict with her indecision . ' ''
`` Jem say that he think they will be leave very soon now , and that he will not be able to get leave to come so far before they go , a they will have to start at a few hour ' notice , '' say the doctor , pass the letter to his wife .
`` That be not fair , '' say Susan indignantly .
`` Has Sir Sam Hughes no regard for our feeling ?
The idea of whisk that bless boy away to Europe without let u even have a last glimpse of him !
If I be you , doctor dear , I would write to the paper about it . ''
`` Perhaps it be as well , '' say the disappointed mother .
`` I do n't believe I could bear another parting from him -- now that I know the war will not be over as soon a we hop when he leave first .
Oh , if only -- but no , I wo n't say it !
Like Susan and Rilla , '' conclude Mrs. Blythe , achieve a laugh , `` I be determine to be a heroine . ''
`` You 're all good stuff , '' say the doctor , `` I 'm proud of my woman folk .
Even Rilla here , my ` lily of the field , ' be run a Red Cross Society full blast and save a little life for Canada .
That 's a good piece of work .
Rilla , daughter of Anne , what be you go to call your war-baby ? ''
`` I 'm wait to hear from Jim Anderson , '' say Rilla .
`` He may want to name his own child . ''
But a the autumn week go by no word come from Jim Anderson , who have never be hear from since he sail from Halifax , and to whom the fate of wife and child seem a matter of indifference .
Eventually Rilla decide to call the baby James , and Susan opine that Kitchener should be add thereto .
So James Kitchener Anderson become the possessor of a name somewhat more imposing than himself .
The Ingleside family promptly shorten it to Jims , but Susan obstinately call him `` Little Kitchener '' and nothing else .
`` Jims be no name for a Christian child , Mrs. Dr. dear , '' she say disapprovingly .
`` Cousin Sophia say it be too flippant , and for once I consider she utter sense , though I would not please her by openly agree with her .
As for the child , he be begin to look something like a baby , and I must admit that Rilla be wonderful with him , though I would not pamper pride by say so to her face .
Mrs. Dr. dear , I shall never , no never , forget the first sight I have of that infant , lie in that big soup tureen , roll up in dirty flannel .
It be not often that Susan Baker be flabbergast , but flabbergast I be then , and that you may tie to .
For one awful moment I think my mind have give way and that I be see vision .
Then think I , ` No , I never heard of anyone have a vision of a soup tureen , so it must be real at least , ' and I pluck up confidence .
When I hear the doctor tell Rilla that she must take care of the baby I think he be joke , for I do not believe for a minute she would or could do it .
But you see what have happen and it be make a woman of her .
When we have to do a thing , Mrs. Dr. dear , we can do it . ''
Susan add another proof to this conclude dictum of hers one day in October .
The doctor and his wife be away .
Rilla be preside over Jims ' afternoon siesta upstairs , purl four and knit one with ceaseless vim .
Susan be seat on the back veranda , shell bean , and Cousin Sophia be help her .
Peace and tranquility brood over the Glen ; the sky be fleece over with silvery , shin cloud .
Rainbow Valley lay in a soft , autumnal haze of fairy purple .
The maple grove be a burn bush of colour and the hedge of sweet-briar around the kitchen yard be a thing of wonder in it subtle tinting .
It do not seem that strife could be in the world , and Susan 's faithful heart be lull into a brief forgetfulness , although she have lie awake most of the precede night thinking of little Jem far out on the Atlantic , where the great fleet be carry Canada 's first army across the ocean .
Even Cousin Sophia look less melancholy than usual and admit that there be not much fault to be find in the day , although there be no doubt it be a weather-breeder and there would be an awful storm on it heel .
`` Things be too calm to last , '' she say .
As if in confirmation of her assertion , a most unearthly din suddenly arise behind them .
It be quite impossible to describe the confused medley of bang and rattle and muffle shriek and yowl that proceed from the kitchen , accompany by occasional crash .
Susan and Cousin Sophia star at each other in dismay .
`` What upon airth have bruk loose in there ? ''
gasp Cousin Sophia .
`` It must be that Hyde-cat go clean mad at last , '' mutter Susan .
`` I have always expect it . ''
Rilla come fly out of the side door of the living-room .
`` What have happen ? ''
she demand .
`` It be beyond me to say , but that possess beast of yours be evidently at the bottom of it , '' say Susan .
`` Do not go near him , at least .
I will open the door and peep in .
There go some more of the crockery .
I have always say that the devil be in him and that I will tie to . ''
`` It be my opinion that the cat have hydrophobia , '' say Cousin Sophia solemnly .
`` I once heard of a cat that go mad and bite three people -- and they all die a most terrible death , and turn black a ink . ''
Undismayed by this , Susan open the door and look in .
The floor be litter with fragment of broken dish , for it seem that the fatal tragedy have take place on the long dresser where Susan 's array of cook bowl have be marshal in shin state .
Around the kitchen tear a frantic cat , with his head wedge tightly in an old salmon can .
Blindly he career about with shriek and profanity commingle , now bang the can madly against anything he encounter , now try vainly to wrench it off with his paw .
The sight be so funny that Rilla double up with laughter .
Susan look at her reproachfully .
`` I see nothing to laugh at .
That beast have break your ma 's big blue mixing-bowl that she bring from Green Gables when she be marry .
That be no small calamity , in my opinion .
But the thing to consider now be how to get that can off Hyde 's head . ''
`` Do n't you dast go touch it , '' exclaim Cousin Sophia , galvanize into animation .
`` It might be your death .
Shut the kitchen up and send for Albert . ''
`` I be not in the habit of send for Albert during family difficulty , '' say Susan loftily .
`` That beast be in torment , and whatever my opinion of him may be , I can not endure to see him suffer pain .
You keep away , Rilla , for little Kitchener 's sake , and I will see what I can do . ''
Susan stalk undauntedly into the kitchen , seize an old storm coat of the doctor 's and after a wild pursuit and several fruitless dash and pounce , manage to throw it over the cat and can .
Then she proceed to saw the can loose with a can-opener , while Rilla hold the squirm animal , roll in the coat .
Anything like Doc 's shriek while the process be go on be never hear at Ingleside .
Susan be in mortal dread that the Albert Crawfords would hear it and conclude she be torture the creature to death .
Doc be a wrathful and indignant cat when he be free .
Evidently he think the whole thing be a put-up job to bring him low .
He give Susan a baleful glance by way of gratitude and rush out of the kitchen to take sanctuary in the jungle of the sweet-briar hedge , where he sulk for the rest of the day .
Susan sweep up her broken dish grimly .
`` The Huns themselves could n't have work more havoc here , '' she say bitterly .
`` But when people will keep a Satanic animal like that , in spite of all warning , they can not complain when their wedding bowl get break .
Things have come to a pretty pas when an honest woman can not leave her kitchen for a few minute without a fiend of a cat rampage through it with his head in a salmon can . ''
CHAPTER X THE TROUBLES OF RILLA October pass out and the dreary day of November and December drag by .
The world shook with the thunder of contend army ; Antwerp fell -- Turkey declare war -- gallant little Serbia gather herself together and strike a deadly blow at her oppressor ; and in quiet , hill-girdled Glen St. Mary , thousand of mile away , heart beat with hope and fear over the vary dispatch from day to day .
`` A few month ago , '' say Miss Oliver , `` we think and talk in term of Glen St. Mary .
Now , we think and talk in term of military tactic and diplomatic intrigue . ''
There be just one great event every day -- the come of the mail .
Even Susan admit that from the time the mail-courier 's buggy rumble over the little bridge between the station and the village until the paper be bring home and read , she could not work properly .
`` I must take up my knitting then and knit hard till the paper come , Mrs. Dr. dear .
Knitting be something you can do , even when your heart be go like a trip-hammer and the pit of your stomach feel all go and your thought be catawampus .
Then when I see the headline , be they good or be they bad , I calm down and be able to go about my business again .
It be an unfortunate thing that the mail come in just when our dinner rush be on , and I think the Government could arrange thing good .
But the drive on Calais have fail , a I felt perfectly sure it would , and the Kaiser will not eat his Christmas dinner in London this year .
Do you know , Mrs. Dr. dear , '' -- Susan 's voice lower a a token that she be go to impart a very shocking piece of information , -- `` I have be tell on good authority -- or else you may be sure I would not be repeat it when it concern a minster -- that the Rev . Mr. Arnold go to Charlottetown every week and take a Turkish bath for his rheumatism .
The idea of him do that when we be at war with Turkey ?
One of his own deacon have always insist that Mr. Arnold 's theology be not sound and I be begin to believe that there be some reason to fear it .
Well , I must bestir myself this afternoon and get little Jem 's Christmas cake pack up for him .
He will enjoy it , if the bless boy be not drown in mud before that time . ''
Jem be in camp on Salisbury Plain and be write gay , cheery letter home in spite of the mud .
Walter be at Redmond and his letter to Rilla be anything but cheerful .
She never open one without a dread tugging at her heart that it would tell her he have enlist .
His unhappiness make her unhappy .
She want to put her arm round him and comfort him , a she have do that day in Rainbow Valley .
She hat everybody who be responsible for Walter 's unhappiness .
`` He will go yet , '' she murmur miserably to herself one afternoon , a she sit alone in Rainbow Valley , read a letter from him , `` he will go yet -- and if he do I just ca n't bear it . ''
Walter write that some one have send him an envelope contain a white feather .
`` I deserve it , Rilla .
I felt that I ought to put it on and wear it -- proclaim myself to all Redmond the coward I know I be .
The boy of my year be go -- go .
Every day two or three of them join up .
Some day I almost make up my mind to do it -- and then I see myself thrust a bayonet through another man -- some woman 's husband or sweetheart or son -- perhaps the father of little child -- I see myself lie alone tear and mangle , burn with thirst on a cold , wet field , surround by dead and die men -- and I know I never can .
I ca n't face even the thought of it .
How could I face the reality ?
There be time when I wish I have never be bear .
Life have always seem such a beautiful thing to me -- and now it be a hideous thing .
Rilla-my-Rilla , if it be n't for your letter -- your dear , bright , merry , funny , comical , believe letter -- I think I 'd give up .
And Una 's !
Una be really a little brick , be n't she ?
There 's a wonderful fineness and firmness under all that shy , wistful girlishness of her .
She have n't your knack of write laugh-provoking epistle , but there 's something in her letter -- I do n't know what -- that make me feel at least while I 'm read them , that I could even go to the front .
Not that she ever say a word about my go -- or hint that I ought to go -- she be n't that kind .
It 's just the spirit of them -- the personality that be in them .
Well , I ca n't go .
You have a brother and Una have a friend who be a coward . ''
`` Oh , I wish Walter would n't write such thing , '' sigh Rilla .
`` It hurt me .
He be n't a coward -- he be n't -- he be n't ! ''
She look wistfully about her -- at the little woodland valley and the grey , lonely fallows beyond .
How everything remind her of Walter !
The red leaf still cling to the wild sweet-briars that overhang a curve of the brook ; their stem be gemmed with the pearl of the gentle rain that have fall a little while before .
Walter have once write a poem describe them .
The wind be sigh and rustle among the frost brown bracken fern , then lessen sorrowfully away down the brook .
Walter have say once that he love the melancholy of the autumn wind on a November day .
The old Tree Lovers still clasp each other in a faithful embrace , and the White Lady , now a great white-branched tree , stand out beautifully fine , against the grey velvet sky .
Walter have name them long ago ; and last November , when he have walk with her and Miss Oliver in the Valley , he have say , look at the leafless Lady , with a young silver moon hanging over her , `` A white birch be a beautiful Pagan maiden who have never lose the Eden secret of be naked and unashamed . ''
Miss Oliver have say , `` Put that into a poem , Walter , '' and he have do so , and read it to them the next day -- just a short thing with goblin imagination in every line of it .
Oh , how happy they have be then !
Well -- Rilla scramble to her foot -- time be up .
Jims would soon be awake -- his lunch have to be prepare -- his little slip have to be iron -- there be a committee meeting of the Junior Reds that night -- there be her new knit bag to finish -- it would be the handsome bag in the Junior Society -- handsomer even than Irene Howard 's -- she must get home and get to work .
She be busy these day from morning till night .
That little monkey of a Jims take so much time .
But he be grow -- he be certainly grow .
And there be time when Rilla felt sure that it be not merely a pious hope but an absolute fact that he be get decidedly well look .
Sometimes she felt quite proud of him ; and sometimes she yearn to spank him .
But she never kiss him or want to kiss him .
`` The Germans capture Lodz today , '' say Miss Oliver , one December evening , when she , Mrs. Blythe , and Susan be busy sew or knit in the cosy living-room .
`` This war be at least extend my knowledge of geography .
Schoolma'am though I be , three month ago I do n't know there be such a place in the world such a Lodz .
Had I hear it mention I would have know nothing about it and care a little .
I know all about it now -- it size , it standing , it military significance .
Yesterday the news that the Germans have capture it in their second rush to Warsaw make my heart sink into my boot .
I wake up in the night and worry over it .
I do n't wonder baby always cry when they wake up in the night .
Everything press on my soul then and no cloud have a silver lining . ''
`` When I wake up in the night and can not go to sleep again , '' remark Susan , who be knit and read at the same time , `` I pass the moment by torture the Kaiser to death .
Last night I fry him in boil oil and a great comfort it be to me , remember those Belgian baby . ''
`` If the Kaiser be here and have a pain in his shoulder you 'd be the first to run for the liniment bottle to rub him down , '' laugh Miss Oliver .
`` Would I ? ''
cry outraged Susan .
`` Would I , Miss Oliver ?
I would rub him down with coal oil , Miss Oliver -- and leave it to blister .
That be what I would do and that you may tie to .
A pain in his shoulder , indeed !
He will have pain all over him before he be through with what he have start . ''
`` We be tell to love our enemy , Susan , '' say the doctor solemnly .
`` Yes , our enemy , but not King George 's enemy , doctor dear , '' retort Susan crushingly .
She be so well pleased with herself over this flatten out of the doctor completely that she even smile a she polish her glass .
Susan have never give in to glass before , but she have do so at last in order to be able to read the war news -- and not a dispatch got by her .
`` Can you tell me , Miss Oliver , how to pronounce M-l-a-w-a and B-z-u-r-a and P-r-z-e-m-y-s-l ? ''
`` That last be a conundrum which nobody seem to have solve yet , Susan .
And I can make only a guess at the others . ''
`` These foreign name be far from be decent , in my opinion , '' say disgust Susan .
`` I dare say the Austrians and Russians would think Saskatchewan and Musquodoboit about as bad , Susan , '' say Miss Oliver .
`` The Serbians have do wonderfully of late .
They have capture Belgrade . ''
`` And send the Austrian creature pack across the Danube with a flea in their ear , '' say Susan with a relish , a she settle down to examine a map of Eastern Europe , prod each locality with the knit needle to brand it on her memory .
`` Cousin Sophia say awhile ago that Serbia be do for , but I tell her there be still such a thing a an over-ruling Providence , doubt it who might .
It say here that the slaughter be terrible .
For all they be foreigner it be awful to think of so many men be kill , Mrs. Dr. dear -- for they be scarce enough a it be . ''
Rilla be upstairs relieve her over-charged feeling by write in her diary .
`` Things have all ` go catawampus , ' a Susan say , with me this week .
Part of it be my own fault and part of it be n't , and I seem to be equally unhappy over both part .
`` I go to town the other day to buy a new winter hat .
It be the first time nobody insist on come with me to help me select it , and I felt that mother have really give up thinking of me a a child .
And I find the dear hat -- it be simply bewitch .
It be a velvet hat , of the very shade of rich green that be make for me .
It just go with my hair and complexion beautifully , bring out the red-brown shade and what Miss Oliver call my ` creaminess ' so well .
Only once before in my life have I come across that precise shade of green .
When I be twelve I have a little beaver hat of it , and all the girl in school be wild over it .
Well , as soon a I saw this hat I felt that I simply must have it -- and have it I do .
The price be dreadful .
I will not put it down here because I do n't want my descendant to know I be guilty of pay so much for a hat , in war-time , too , when everybody be -- or should be -- try to be economical .
`` When I get home and try on the hat again in my room I be assail by qualm .
Of course , it be very become ; but somehow it seem too elaborate and fussy for church go and our quiet little doings in the Glen -- too conspicuous , in short .
It have n't seem so at the milliner 's but here in my little white room it do .
And that dreadful price tag !
And the starving Belgians !
When mother saw the hat and the tag she just look at me .
Mother be some expert at look .
Father say she look him into love with her year ago in Avonlea school and I can well believe it -- though I have hear a weird tale of her banging him over the head with a slate at the very begin of their acquaintance .
Mother be a limb when she be a little girl , I understand , and even up to the time when Jem go away she be full of ginger .
But let me return to my mutton -- that be to say , my new green velvet hat . ''
` Do you think , Rilla , ' mother say quietly -- far too quietly -- ` that it be right to spend so much for a hat , especially when the need of the world be so great ? ' '' '
I pay for it out of my own allowance , mother , ' I exclaim . ''
` That be not the point .
Your allowance be base on the principle of a reasonable amount for each thing you need .
If you pay too much for one thing you must cut off somewhere else and that be not satisfactory .
But if you think you do right , Rilla , I have no more to say .
I leave it to your conscience . '
`` I wish mother would not leave thing to my conscience !
And anyway , what be I to do ?
I could n't take that hat back -- I have wear it to a concert in town -- I have to keep it !
I be so uncomfortable that I fly into a temper -- a cold , calm , deadly temper . ''
` Mother , ' I say haughtily , ' I be sorry you disapprove of my hat -- ' '' ` Not of the hat exactly , ' say mother , ` though I consider it in doubtful taste for so young a girl -- but of the price you pay for it . '
`` Being interrupt do n't improve my temper , so I go on , colder and calmer and deadlier than ever , just a if mother have not speak . '' '
-- but I have to keep it now .
However , I promise you that I will not get another hat for three year or for the duration of the war , if it last long than that .
Even you ' -- oh , the sarcasm I put into the ` you ' -- ` can not say that what I pay be too much when spread over at least three year . ' ''
` You will be very tired of that hat before three year , Rilla , ' say mother , with a provoking grin , which , be interpret , mean that I would n't stick it out . ''
` Tired or not , I will wear it that long , ' I say : and then I march upstairs and cry to think that I have be sarcastic to mother .
`` I hate that hat already .
But three year or the duration of the war , I say , and three year or the duration of the war it shall be .
I vow and I shall keep my vow , cost what it will .
`` That be one of the ` catawampus ' thing .
The other be that I have quarrel with Irene Howard -- or she quarrel with me -- or , no , we both quarrel .
`` The Junior Red Cross meet here yesterday .
The hour of meeting be half-past two but Irene come at half-past one , because she get the chance of a drive down from the Upper Glen .
Irene have n't be a bit nice to me since the fuss about the eats ; and besides I feel sure she resent not be president .
But I have be determine that thing should go smoothly , so I have never take any notice , and when she come yesterday she seem so nice and sweet again that I hop she have get over her huffiness and we could be the chum we use to be .
`` But as soon a we sit down Irene begin to rub me the wrong way .
I saw her cast a look at my new knitting-bag .
All the girl have always say Irene be jealous-minded and I would never believe them before .
But now I feel that perhaps she be .
`` The first thing she do be to pounce on Jims -- Irene pretend to adore baby -- pick him out of his cradle and kiss him all over his face .
Now , Irene know perfectly well that I do n't like to have Jims kiss like that .
It be not hygienic .
After she have worry him till he begin to fuss , she look at me and give quite a nasty little laugh but she say , oh , so sweetly , '' ` Why , Rilla , darling , you look a if you think I be poison the baby . ' ''
` Oh , no , I do n't , Irene , ' I say -- every bit a sweetly , ` but you know Morgan say that the only place a baby should be kiss be on it forehead , for fear of germ , and that be my rule with Jims . ' ''
` Dear me , be I so full of germ ? '
say Irene plaintively .
I know she be make fun of me and I begin to boil inside -- but outside no sign of a simmer .
I be determine I would not scrap with Irene .
`` Then she begin to bounce Jims .
Now , Morgan say bouncing be almost the bad thing that can be do to a baby .
I never allow Jims to be bounce .
But Irene bounce him and that exasperate child like it .
He smile -- for the very first time .
He be four month old and he have never smile once before .
Not even mother or Susan have be able to coax that thing to smile , try a they would .
And here he be smile because Irene Howard bounce him !
Talk of gratitude !
`` I admit that smile make a big difference in him .
Two of the dear dimple come out in his cheek and his big brown eye seem full of laughter .
The way Irene rave over those dimple be silly , I consider .
You would have suppose she think she have really bring them into existence .
But I sew steadily and do not enthuse , and soon Irene get tire of bounce Jims and put him back in his cradle .
He do not like that after be play with , and he begin to cry and be fussy the rest of the afternoon , whereas if Irene have only leave him alone he would not have be a bit of trouble .
`` Irene look at him and say , ` Does he often cry like that ? '
a if she have never hear a baby cry before .
`` I explain patiently that child have to cry so many minute per day in order to expand their lung .
Morgan say so . ''
` If Jims do n't cry at all I 'd have to make him cry for at least twenty minute , ' I say . ''
` Oh , indeed ! '
say Irene , laugh a if she do n't believe me .
` Morgan on the Care of Infants ' be upstairs or I would soon have convince her .
Then she say Jims do n't have much hair -- she have never see a four month ' old baby so bald .
`` Of course , I know Jims have n't much hair -- yet ; but Irene say it in a tone that seem to imply it be my fault that he have n't any hair .
I say I have see dozen of baby every bit as bald a Jims , and Irene say , Oh very well , she have n't mean to offend me -- when I be n't offend .
`` It go on like that the rest of the hour -- Irene keep give me little dig all the time .
The girl have always say she be revengeful like that if she be peeve about anything ; but I never believe it before ; I use to think Irene just perfect , and it hurt me dreadfully to find she could stoop to this .
But I cork up my feeling and sew away for dear life on a Belgian child 's nightgown .
`` Then Irene tell me the mean , most contemptible thing that someone have say about Walter .
I wo n't write it down -- I ca n't .
Of course , she say it make her furious to hear it and all that -- but there be no need for her to tell me such a thing even if she do hear it .
She simply do it to hurt me .
`` I just explode .
` How dare you come here and repeat such a thing about my brother , Irene Howard ? '
I exclaim . '
I shall never forgive you -- never .
Your brother have n't enlist -- have n't any idea of enlist . ' ''
` Why Rilla , dear , I do n't say it , ' say Irene . '
I tell you it be Mrs. George Burr .
And I tell her -- ' '' ' I do n't want to hear what you tell her .
Do n't you ever speak to me again , Irene Howard . '
`` Oh course , I should n't have say that .
But it just seem to say itself .
Then the other girl all come in a bunch and I have to calm down and act the hostess ' part as well a I could .
Irene pair off with Olive Kirk all the rest of the afternoon and go away without so much a a look .
So I suppose she mean to take me at my word and I do n't care , for I do not want to be friend with a girl who could repeat such a falsehood about Walter .
But I feel unhappy over it for all that .
We 've always be such good chum and until lately Irene be lovely to me ; and now another illusion have be strip from my eye and I feel a if there be n't such a thing a real true friendship in the world .
`` Father get old Joe Mead to build a kennel for Dog Monday in the corner of the shipping-shed today .
We think perhaps Monday would come home when the cold weather come but he would n't .
No earthly influence can coax Monday away from that shed even for a few minute .
There he stay and meet every train .
So we have to do something to make him comfortable .
Joe build the kennel so that Monday could lie in it and still see the platform , so we hope he will occupy it .
`` Monday have become quite famous .
A reporter of the Enterprise come out from town and photograph him and write up the whole story of his faithful vigil .
It be publish in the Enterprise and copy all over Canada .
But that do n't matter to poor little Monday , Jem have go away -- Monday do n't know where or why -- but he will wait until he come back .
Somehow it comfort me : it 's foolish , I suppose , but it give me a feeling that Jem will come back or else Monday would n't keep on wait for him .
`` Jims be snore beside me in his cradle .
It be just a cold that make him snore -- not adenoid .
Irene have a cold yesterday and I know she give it to him , kiss him .
He be not quite such a nuisance a he be ; he have get some backbone and can sit up quite nicely , and he love his bath now and splash unsmilingly in the water instead of twist and shriek .
Oh , shall I ever forget those first two month !
I do n't know how I live through them .
But here I be and here be Jims and we both be go to ` carry on . '
I tickle him a little bit tonight when I undress him -- I would n't bounce him but Morgan do n't mention tickle -- just to see if he would smile for me as well a Irene .
And he do -- and out pop the dimple .
What a pity his mother could n't have see them !
`` I finish my sixth pair of sock today .
With the first three I get Susan to set the heel for me .
Then I think that be a bit of shirking , so I learn to do it myself .
I hate it -- but I have do so many thing I hate since 4th of August that one more or less do n't matter .
I just think of Jem joke about the mud on Salisbury Plain and I go at them . ''
CHAPTER XI DARK AND BRIGHT At Christmas the college boy and girl come home and for a little while Ingleside be gay again .
But all be not there -- for the first time one be miss from the circle round the Christmas table .
Jem , of the steady lip and fearless eye , be far away , and Rilla felt that the sight of his vacant chair be more than she could endure .
Susan have take a stubborn freak and insist on set out Jem 's place for him as usual , with the twisted little napkin ring he have always have since a boy , and the odd , high Green Gables goblet that Aunt Marilla have once give him and from which he always insist on drinking .
`` That bless boy shall have his place , Mrs. Dr. dear , '' say Susan firmly , `` and do not you feel over it , for you may be sure he be here in spirit and next Christmas he will be here in the body .
Wait you till the Big Push come in the spring and the war will be over in a jiffy . ''
They try to think so , but a shadow stalk in the background of their determined merrymaking .
Walter , too , be quiet and dull , all through the holiday .
He show Rilla a cruel , anonymous letter he have receive at Redmond -- a letter far more conspicuous for malice than for patriotic indignation .
`` Nevertheless , all it say be true , Rilla . ''
Rilla have catch it from him and throw it into the fire .
`` There be n't one word of truth in it , '' she declare hotly .
`` Walter , you 've get morbid -- a Miss Oliver say she get when she brood too long over one thing . ''
`` I ca n't get away from it at Redmond , Rilla .
The whole college be aflame over the war .
A perfectly fit fellow , of military age , who do n't join up be looked upon a a shirker and treat accordingly .
Dr. Milne , the English professor , who have always make a special pet of me , have two son in khaki ; and I can feel the change in his manner towards me . ''
`` It 's not fair -- you 're not fit . ''
`` Physically I be .
Sound a a bell .
The unfitness be in the soul and it 's a taint and a disgrace .
There , do n't cry , Rilla .
I 'm not go if that 's what you 're afraid of .
The Piper 's music ring in my ear day and night -- but I can not follow . ''
`` You would break mother 's heart and mine if you do , '' sob Rilla .
`` Oh , Walter , one be enough for any family . ''
The holiday be an unhappy time for her .
Still , have Nan and Di and Walter and Shirley home help in the enduring of thing .
A letter and book come for her from Kenneth Ford , too ; some sentence in the letter make her cheeks burn and her heart beat -- until the last paragraph , which send an icy chill over everything .
`` My ankle be about as good a new .
I 'll be fit to join up in a couple of month more , Rilla-my-Rilla .
It will be some feeling to get into khaki all right .
Little Ken will be able to look the whole world in the face then and owe not any man .
It 's be rotten lately , since I 've be able to walk without limp .
People who do n't know look at me as much a to say ` Slacker ! '
Well , they wo n't have the chance to look it much longer . ''
`` I hate this war , '' say Rilla bitterly , a she gaze out into the maple grove that be a chill glory of pink and gold in the winter sunset .
`` Nineteen-fourteen have go , '' say Dr. Blythe on New Year 's Day .
`` Its sun , which rise fairly , have set in blood .
What will nineteen-fifteen bring ? ''
`` Victory ! ''
say Susan , for once laconic .
`` Do you really believe we 'll win the war , Susan ? ''
say Miss Oliver drearily .
She have come over from Lowbridge to spend the day and see Walter and the girl before they go back to Redmond .
She be in a rather blue and cynical mood and incline to look on the dark side . ''
` Believe ' we 'll win the war ! ''
exclaim Susan .
`` No , Miss Oliver , dear , I do not believe -- I know .
That do not worry me .
What do worry me be the trouble and expense of it all .
But then you can not make omelet without break egg , so we must just trust in God and make big gun . ''
`` Sometimes I think the big gun be well to trust in than God , '' say Miss Oliver defiantly .
`` No , no , dear , you do not .
The Germans have the big gun at the Marne , have they not ?
But Providence settle them .
Do not ever forget that .
Just hold on to that when you feel incline to doubt .
Clutch hold of the side of your chair and sit tight and keep say , ` Big gun be good but the Almighty be well , and He be on our side , no matter what the Kaiser say about it . '
I would have go crazy many a day lately , Miss Oliver , dear , if I have not sit tight and repeat that to myself .
My cousin Sophia be , like you , somewhat inclined to despond .
` Oh , dear me , what will we do if the Germans ever get here , ' she wail to me yesterday .
` Bury them , ' say I , just as off-hand a that .
` There be plenty of room for the graf . '
Cousin Sophia say that I be flippant but I be not flippant , Miss Oliver , dear , only calm and confident in the British navy and our Canadian boy .
I be like old Mr. William Pollock of the Harbour Head .
He be very old and have be ill for a long time , and one night last week he be so low that his daughter-in-law whisper to some one that she think he be dead .
` Darn it , I ai n't , ' he call right out -- only , Miss Oliver , dear , he do not use so mild a word a ` darn ' -- ` darn it , I ai n't , and I do n't mean to die until the Kaiser be well lick . '
Now , that , Miss Oliver , dear , '' conclude Susan , `` be the kind of spirit I admire . ''
`` I admire it but I ca n't emulate it , '' sigh Gertrude .
`` Before this , I have always be able to escape from the hard thing of life for a little while by go into dreamland , and come back like a giant refreshed .
But I ca n't escape from this . ''
`` Nor I , '' say Mrs. Blythe .
`` I hate go to bed now .
All my life I 've like go to bed , to have a gay , mad , splendid half-hour of imagine thing before sleep .
Now I imagine them still .
But such different thing . ''
`` I be rather glad when the time come to go to bed , '' say Miss Oliver .
`` I like the darkness because I can be myself in it -- I need n't smile or talk bravely .
But sometimes my imagination get out of hand , too , and I see what you do -- terrible thing -- terrible year to come . ''
`` I be very thankful that I never have any imagination to speak of , '' say Susan .
`` I have be spar that .
I see by this paper that the Crown Prince be kill again .
Do you suppose there be any hope of his stay dead this time ?
And I also see that Woodrow Wilson be go to write another note .
I wonder , '' conclude Susan , with the bitter irony she have of late begin to use when refer to the poor President , `` if that man 's schoolmaster be alive . ''
In January Jims be five month old and Rilla celebrate the anniversary by shorten him .
`` He weigh fourteen pound , '' she announce jubilantly .
`` Just exactly what he should weigh at five month , accord to Morgan . ''
There be no longer any doubt in anybody 's mind that Jims be get positively pretty .
His little cheek be round and firm and faintly pink , his eye be big and bright , his tiny paw have dimple at the root of every finger .
He have even begin to grow hair , much to Rilla 's unspoken relief .
There be a pale golden fuzz all over his head that be distinctly visible in some light .
He be a good infant , generally sleep and digest a Morgan decreed .
Occasionally he smile but he have never laugh , in spite of all effort to make him .
This worried Rilla also , because Morgan say that baby usually laugh aloud from the third to the fifth month .
Jims be five month and have no notion of laughing .
Why have n't he ?
Was n't he normal ?
One night Rilla come home late from a recruiting meeting at the Glen where she have be give patriotic recitation .
Rilla have never be willing to recite in public before .
She be afraid of her tendency to lisp , which have a habit of revive if she be do anything that make her nervous .
When she have first be ask to recite at the Upper Glen meeting she have refuse .
Then she begin to worry over her refusal .
Was it cowardly ?
What would Jem think if he know ?
After two day of worry Rilla phone to the president of the Patriotic Society that she would recite .
She do , and lisp several time , and lay awake most of the night in an agony of wounded vanity .
Then two night after she recite again at Harbour Head .
She have be at Lowbridge and over-harbour since then and have become resign to an occasional lisp .
Nobody except herself seem to mind it .
And she be so earnest and appeal and shining-eyed !
More than one recruit join up because Rilla 's eye seem to look right at him when she passionately demand how could men die good than fight for the ash of their father and the temple of their god , or assure her audience with thrill intensity that one crowd hour of glorious life be worth an age without a name .
Even stolid Miller Douglas be so fired one night that it take Mary Vance a good hour to talk him back to sense .
Mary Vance say bitterly that if Rilla Blythe felt as bad a she have pretend to feel over Jem 's go to the front she would n't be urge other girl ' brother and friend to go .
On this particular night Rilla be tire and cold and very thankful to creep into her warm nest and cuddle down between her blanket , though a usual with a sorrowful wonder how Jem and Jerry be fare .
She be just get warm and drowsy when Jims suddenly begin to cry -- and keep on cry .
Rilla curl herself up in her bed and determine she would let him cry .
She have Morgan behind her for justification .
Jims be warm , physically comfortable -- his cry be n't the cry of pain -- and have his little tummy as full a be good for him .
Under such circumstance it would be simply spoil him to fuss over him , and she be n't go to do it .
He could cry until he get good and tired and ready to go to sleep again .
Then Rilla 's imagination begin to torment her .
Suppose , she think , I be a tiny , helpless creature only five month old , with my father somewhere in France and my poor little mother , who have be so worried about me , in the graveyard .
Suppose I be lie in a basket in a big , black room , without one speck of light , and nobody within mile of me , for all I could see or know .
Suppose there be n't a human be anywhere who love me -- for a father who have never see me could n't love me very much , especially when he have never write a word to or about me .
Would n't I cry , too ?
Would n't I feel just so lonely and forsaken and frighten that I 'd have to cry ?
Rilla hop out .
She pick Jims out of his basket and take him into her own bed .
His hand be cold , poor mite .
But he have promptly cease to cry .
And then , a she hold him close to her in the darkness , suddenly Jims laugh -- a real , gurgly , chuckly , delight , delightful laugh .
`` Oh , you dear little thing ! ''
exclaim Rilla .
`` Are you so pleased at find you 're not all alone , lose in a huge , big , black room ? ''
Then she know she want to kiss him and she do .
She kiss his silky , scent little head , she kiss his chubby little cheek , she kiss his little cold hand .
She want to squeeze him -- to cuddle him , just a she use to squeeze and cuddle her kitten .
Something delightful and yearning and brooding seem to have take possession of her .
She have never felt like this before .
In a few minute Jims be sound asleep ; and , a Rilla listen to his soft , regular breathing and felt the little body warm and contented against her , she realize that -- at last -- she love her war-baby .
`` He have get to be -- such -- a -- darling , '' she think drowsily , a she drift off to slumberland herself .
In February Jem and Jerry and Robert Grant be in the trench and a little more tension and dread be add to the Ingleside life .
In March `` Yiprez , '' a Susan call it , have come to have a bitter significance .
The daily list of casualty have begin to appear in the paper and no one at Ingleside ever answer the telephone without a horrible cold shrinking -- for it might be the station-master phone up to say a telegram have come from overseas .
No one at Ingleside ever get up in the morning without a sudden piercing wonder over what the day might bring .
`` And I use to welcome the morning so , '' think Rilla .
Yet the round of life and duty go steadily on and every week or so one of the Glen lad who have just the other day be a rollick schoolboy go into khaki .
`` It be bitter cold out tonight , Mrs. Dr. dear , '' say Susan , come in out of the clear starlit crispness of the Canadian winter twilight .
`` I wonder if the boy in the trench be warm . ''
`` How everything come back to this war , '' cry Gertrude Oliver .
`` We ca n't get away from it -- not even when we talk of the weather .
I never go out these dark cold night myself without thinking of the men in the trench -- not only our men but everybody 's men .
I would feel the same if there be nobody I know at the front .
When I snuggle down in my comfortable bed I be ashamed of be comfortable .
It seem a if it be wicked of me to be so when many be not . ''
`` I saw Mrs. Meredith down at the store , '' say Susan , `` and she tell me that they be really troubled over Bruce , he take thing so much to heart .
He have cry himself to sleep for a week , over the starving Belgians .
` Oh , mother , ' he will say to her , so beseeching-like , ` surely the baby be never hungry -- oh , not the baby , mother !
Just say the baby be not hungry , mother . '
And she can not say it because it would not be true , and she be at her wit ' end .
They try to keep such thing from him but he find them out and then they can not comfort him .
It break my heart to read about them myself , Mrs. Dr. dear , and I can not console myself with the thought that the tale be not true .
When I read a novel that make me want to weep I just say severely to myself , ` Now , Susan Baker , you know that be all a pack of lie . '
But we must carry on .
Jack Crawford say he be go to the war because he be tire of farming .
I hope he will find it a pleasant change .
And Mrs. Richard Elliott over-harbour be worry herself sick because she use to be always scold her husband about smoke up the parlour curtain .
Now that he have enlist she wish she have never say a word to him .
You know Josiah Cooper and William Daley , Mrs. Dr. dear .
They use to be fast friend but they quarrel twenty year ago and have never speak since .
Well , the other day Josiah go to William and say right out , ` Let u be friend .
` Tai n't any time to be hold grudge . '
William be real glad and hold out his hand , and they sit down for a good talk .
And in less than half an hour they have quarrel again , over how the war ought to be fight , Josiah hold that the Dardanelles expedition be rank folly and William maintain that it be the one sensible thing the Allies have do .
And now they be madder at each other than ever and William say Josiah be a bad a pro-German a Whiskers-on-the-Moon .
Whiskers-on-the-moon vow he be no pro-German but call himself a pacifist , whatever that may be .
It be nothing proper or Whiskers would not be it and that you may tie to .
He say that the big British victory at New Chapelle cost more than it be worth and he have forbid Joe Milgrave to come near the house because Joe run up his father 's flag when the news come .
Have you notice , Mrs. Dr. dear , that the Czar have change that Prish name to Premysl , which prove that the man have good sense , Russian though he be ?
Joe Vickers tell me in the store that he saw a very queer look thing in the sky tonight over Lowbridge way .
Do you suppose it could have be a Zeppelin , Mrs. Dr. dear ? ''
`` I do not think it very likely , Susan . ''
`` Well , I would feel easy about it if Whiskers-on-the-moon be not live in the Glen .
They say he be see go through strange manoeuvre with a lantern in his back yard one night lately .
Some people think he be signal . ''
`` To whom -- or what ? ''
`` Ah , that be the mystery , Mrs. Dr. dear .
In my opinion the Government would do well to keep an eye on that man if it do not want u to be all murder in our bed some night .
Now I shall just look over the paper a minute before go to write a letter to little Jem .
Two thing I never do , Mrs. Dr. dear , be write letter and read politics .
Yet here I be do both regular and I find there be something in politics after all .
Whatever Woodrow Wilson mean I can not fathom but I be hop I will puzzle it out yet . ''
Susan , in her pursuit of Wilson and politics , presently come upon something that disturb her and exclaim in a tone of bitter disappointment , `` That devilish Kaiser have only a boil after all . ''
`` Do n't swear , Susan , '' say Dr. Blythe , pull a long face . ''
` Devilish ' be not swearing , doctor , dear .
I have always understand that swearing be take the name of the Almighty in vain ? ''
`` Well , it be n't -- ahem -- refine , '' say the doctor , wink at Miss Oliver .
`` No , doctor , dear , the devil and the Kaiser -- if so be that they be really two different people -- be not refine .
And you can not refer to them in a refined way .
So I abide by what I say , although you may notice that I be careful not to use such expression when young Rilla be about .
And I maintain that the paper have no right to say that the Kaiser have pneumonia and raise people 's hope , and then come out and say he have nothing but a boil .
A boil , indeed !
I wish he be cover with them . ''
Susan stalk out to the kitchen and settle down to write to Jem ; deem him in need of some home comfort from certain passage in his letter that day .
`` We 're in an old wine cellar tonight , dad , '' he write , `` in water to our knee .
Rats everywhere -- no fire -- a drizzling rain come down -- rather dismal .
But it might be bad .
I get Susan 's box today and everything be in tip-top order and we have a feast .
Jerry be up the line somewhere and he say the ration be rather bad than Aunt Martha 's ditto use to be .
But here they 're not bad -- only monotonous .
Tell Susan I 'd give a year 's pay for a good batch of her monkey-faces ; but do n't let that inspire her to send any for they would n't keep .
`` We have be under fire since the last week in February .
One boy -- he be a Nova Scotian -- be kill right beside me yesterday .
A shell burst near u and when the mess clear away he be lie dead -- not mangle at all -- he just look a little startled .
It be the first time I 'd be close to anything like that and it be a nasty sensation , but one soon get use to horror here .
We 're in an absolutely different world .
The only thing that be the same be the star -- and they be never in their right place , somehow .
`` Tell mother not to worry -- I 'm all right -- fit a a fiddle -- and glad I come .
There 's something across from u here that have get to be wipe out of the world , that 's all -- an emanation of evil that would otherwise poison life for ever .
It 's get to be do , dad , however long it take , and whatever it cost , and you tell the Glen people this for me .
They do n't realize yet what it be have break loose -- I do n't when I first join up .
I think it be fun .
Well , it be n't !
But I 'm in the right place all right -- make no mistake about that .
When I saw what have be do here to home and garden and people -- well , dad , I seem to see a gang of Huns march through Rainbow Valley and the Glen , and the garden at Ingleside .
There be garden over here -- beautiful garden with the beauty of century -- and what be they now ?
Mangled , desecrated thing !
We be fight to make those dear old place where we have play a child , safe for other boy and girl -- fight for the preservation and safety of all sweet , wholesome thing .
`` Whenever any of you go to the station be sure to give Dog Monday a double pat for me .
Fancy the faithful little beggar wait there for me like that !
Honestly , dad , on some of these dark cold night in the trench , it hearten and brace me up no end to think that thousand of mile away at the old Glen station there be a small spotted dog share my vigil .
`` Tell Rilla I 'm glad her war-baby be turn out so well , and tell Susan that I 'm fight a good fight against both Huns and cootie . ''
`` Mrs. Dr. dear , '' whisper Susan solemnly , `` what be cootie ? ''
Mrs. Blythe whisper back and then say in reply to Susan 's horrified ejaculation , `` It 's always like that in the trench , Susan . ''
Susan shake her head and go away in grim silence to re-open a parcel she have sew up for Jem and slip in a fine tooth comb .
CHAPTER XII IN THE DAYS OF LANGEMARCK `` How can spring come and be beautiful in such a horror , '' write Rilla in her diary .
`` When the sun shine and the fluffy yellow catkin be come out on the willow-trees down by the brook , and the garden be begin to be beautiful I ca n't realize that such dreadful thing be happen in Flanders .
But they be !
`` This past week have be terrible for u all , since the news come of the fight around Ypres and the battle of Langemarck and St. Julien .
Our Canadian boy have do splendidly -- General French say they ` save the situation , ' when the Germans have all but break through .
But I ca n't feel pride or exultation or anything but a gnawing anxiety over Jem and Jerry and Mr. Grant .
The casualty list be come out in the paper every day -- oh , there be so many of them .
I ca n't bear to read them for fear I 'd find Jem 's name -- for there have be case where people have see their boy ' name in the casualty list before the official telegram come .
As for the telephone , for a day or two I just refuse to answer it , because I think I could not endure the horrible moment that come between say ` Hello ' and hear the response .
That moment seem a hundred year long , for I be always dread to hear ` There be a telegram for Dr. Blythe . '
Then , when I have shirk for a while , I be ashamed of leave it all for mother or Susan , and now I make myself go .
But it never get any easy .
Gertrude teach school and read composition and set examination paper just a she always have do , but I know her thought be over in Flanders all the time .
Her eye haunt me .
`` And Kenneth be in khaki now , too .
He have get a lieutenant 's commission and expect to go overseas in midsummer , so he write me .
There be n't much else in the letter -- he seem to be think of nothing but go overseas .
I shall not see him again before he go -- perhaps I will never see him again .
Sometimes I ask myself if that evening at Four Winds be all a dream .
It might as well be -- it seem a if it happen in another life live year ago -- and everybody have forget it but me .
`` Walter and Nan and Di come home last night from Redmond .
When Walter step off the train Dog Monday rush to meet him , frantic with joy .
I suppose he think Jem would be there , too .
After the first moment , he pay no attention to Walter and his pat , but just stand there , wag his tail nervously and look past Walter at the other people come out , with eye that make me choke up , for I could n't help think that , for all we know , Monday might never see Jem come off that train again .
Then , when all the people be out , Monday look up at Walter , give his hand a little lick a if to say , ' I know it be n't your fault he do n't come -- excuse me for feel disappointed , ' and then he trot back to his shed , with that funny little sidelong waggle of his that always make it seem that his hind leg be travel directly away from the point at which his foreleg be aim .
`` We try to coax him home with u -- Di even get down and kiss him between the eye and say , ` Monday , old duck , wo n't you come up with u just for the evening ? '
And Monday say -- he do !
-- ' I be very sorry but I ca n't .
I 've get a date to meet Jem here , you know , and there 's a train go through at eight . '
`` It 's lovely to have Walter back again though he seem quiet and sad , just a he be at Christmas .

You have spunk -- I think you would feel so badly over Walter 's enlist that you 'd hardly be able to bear up at all , and here you be as cool a a cucumber .
I wish I have half your nerve . ''
Rilla stand perfectly still .
She felt no emotion whatever -- she felt nothing .
The world of feeling have just go blank .

`` Why , do n't you know ?
I think you do of course , or I would n't have mention it .
I be always put my foot in it , be n't I ?

And then come the awful thought that perhaps she could bear it and that there might be year of this hideous suffering before her .
She must get away -- she must rush home -- she must be alone .
She could not go out there and play for drill and give reading and take part in dialogue now .

Was this she , Rilla Blythe -- this tortured thing , who have be quite happy a few minute ago ?

But no tear come !
Where be her scarf and coat ?
She must get away and hide herself like an animal hurt to the death .
Was it a coward 's part to run away like this ?
The question come to her suddenly a if someone else have ask it .
She think of the shamble of the Flanders front -- she think of her brother and her playmate help to hold those fire-swept trench .
What would they think of her if she shirk her little duty here -- the humble duty of carry the programme through for her Red Cross ?
But she could n't stay -- she could n't -- yet what be it mother have say when Jem go : `` When our woman fail in courage shall our men be fearless still ? ''

Could she go out there and play for it ?

`` That 's good , '' Rilla say mechanically .
Then she be away from them all -- oh , thank God , she be away from them all -- Walter be wait for her at the door .
He put his arm through hers silently and they go together down the moonlit road .
The frog be sing in the marsh , the dim , ensilvered field of home lay all around them .
The spring night be lovely and appeal .
Rilla felt that it beauty be an insult to her pain .
She would hate moonlight for ever .
`` You know ? ''
say Walter .
`` Yes .
Irene tell me , '' answer Rilla chokingly .
`` We do n't want you to know till the evening be over .

`` There be -- plenty -- without you . ''
`` That be n't the point , Rilla-my-Rilla .
I 'm go for my own sake -- to save my soul alive .
It will shrink to something small and mean and lifeless if I do n't go .

There 's so much hideousness in this war -- I 've get to go and help wipe it out of the world .

She must know the bad at once .

`` Oh , I will try . ''

It may come to it full stature in an hour .

`` Our boy give only themselves .
We give them . ''

`` No , no , Susan .

`` Yes , Mrs. Dr. dear .
The doctor tell me last night .

ask the doctor , pause on the threshold .

CHAPTER XV UNTIL THE DAY BREAK `` The Germans have recapture Premysl , '' say Susan despairingly , look up from her newspaper , `` and now I suppose we will have to begin call it by that uncivilised name again .

I say to her , ` My knowledge of geography be not so profound a I wish it be but I have an idea that it be quite a walk from Premysl to Petrograd . '

They have plenty of room for retreat , have they not ? '
