Nobody else like it either ; but all summer the Russian retreat go on -- a long-drawn-out agony .
`` I wonder if I shall ever again be able to await the come of the mail with feeling of composure -- never to speak of pleasure , '' say Gertrude Oliver .
`` The thought that haunt me night and day be -- will the Germans smash Russia completely and then hurl their eastern army , flush with victory , against the western front ? ''
`` They will not , Miss Oliver dear , '' say Susan , assume the role of prophetess .
`` In the first place , the Almighty will not allow it , in the second , Grand Duke Nicholas , though he may have be a disappointment to u in some respect , know how to run away decently and in order , and that be a very useful knowledge when Germans be chase you .
Norman Douglas declare he be just lure them on and kill ten of them to one he lose .
But I be of the opinion he can not help himself and be just do the best he can under the circumstance , the same a the rest of u .
So do not go so far afield to borrow trouble , Miss Oliver dear , when there be plenty of it already camp on our very doorstep . ''
Walter have go to Kingsport the first of June .
Nan , Di and Faith have go also to do Red Cross work in their vacation .
In mid-July Walter come home for a week 's leave before go overseas .
Rilla have live through the day of his absence on the hope of that week , and now that it have come she drink every minute of it thirstily , hat even the hour she have to spend in sleep , they seem such a waste of precious moment .

He be all her own and she know that he find strength and comfort in her sympathy and understanding .

Rainbow Valley be roof over with a sunset of unusual splendour that night ; a wonderful grey dusk just touch with starlight follow it ; and then come moonshine , hint , hiding , revealing , light up little dell and hollow here , leave others in dark , velvet shadow .

The balsam of the fir-trees ; the peace of those white pool of moonshine ; the ` strength of the hill ' -- what a beautiful old Biblical phrase that be .
Rilla !
Look at those old hill around u -- the hill we look up at a child , wonder what lay for u in the great world beyond them .

`` We wo n't be -- happy -- in the same way , '' say Rilla .
`` No , not in the same way .

`` And Ken 's in khaki , too .

She could see a light in Una Meredith 's window .
She felt tempted to say something -- then she know she must not .
It be not her secret : and , anyway , she do not know -- she only suspect .

What fun they all have have here lang syne .
Phantoms of memory seem to pace the dappled path and peep merrily through the swinging bough -- Jem and Jerry , bare-legged , sunburned schoolboy , fishing in the brook and fry trout over the old stone fireplace ; Nan and Di and Faith , in their dimpled , fresh-eyed childish beauty ; Una the sweet and shy , Carl , pore over ant and bug , little slangy , sharp-tongued , good-hearted Mary Vance -- the old Walter that have be himself lie on the grass reading poetry or wander through palace of fancy .

`` Where be you , Walter , '' cry Rilla , laugh a little .

He stand up and look about him at the beautiful valley of moonlight , a if to impress on his mind and heart every charm it possess -- the great dark plume of the fir against the silvery sky , the stately White Lady , the old magic of the dancing brook , the faithful Tree Lovers , the beckoning , tricksy path .

They go back to Ingleside .
Mr. and Mrs. Meredith be there , with Gertrude Oliver , who have come from Lowbridge to say good-bye .

`` There have be many day in the past when I do n't believe in God -- not a God -- only a the impersonal Great First Cause of the scientist .

` Our help in age past ' -- ` the same yesterday , to-day and for ever , ' '' say the minister gently .
`` When we forget God -- He remember u . ''
There be no crowd at the Glen Station the next morning to see Walter off .
It be become a commonplace for a khaki clad boy to board that early morning train after his last leave .
Besides his own , only the Manse folk be there , and Mary Vance .
Mary have send her Miller off the week before , with a determined grin , and now consider herself entitle to give expert opinion on how such parting should be conduct .

CHAPTER XVI REALISM AND ROMANCE `` Warsaw have fall , '' say Dr. Blythe with a resigned air , a he bring the mail in one warm August day .

They have think they be quite resign to Warsaw 's fall but now they know they have , a always , hop against hope .

Then the telephone-bell rang .
There be nothing unusual about the telephone ringing .

`` Hello , be this Ingleside ? ''
`` Yes . ''
`` That you , Rilla ? ''
`` Yeth -- yeth . ''
Oh , why could n't Jims stop howl for just one little minute ?
Why do n't somebody come in and choke him ?
`` Know who 's speak ? ''
Oh , do n't she know !
Would n't she know that voice anywhere -- at any time ?
`` It 's Ken -- be n't it ? ''
`` Sure thing .
I 'm here for a look-in .

Had he use `` you '' in the singular or plural sense ?

`` See here , Rilla , can you arrange that there wo n't be more than a few dozen people round ?
Understand ?
I ca n't make my meaning clearer over this bally rural line .

Did she understand !
Yes , she understand .
`` I 'll try , '' she say .
`` I 'll be up about eight then .
By-by . ''
Rilla hang up the ` phone and fly to Jims .
But she do not wring that injured infant 's neck .

CHAPTER XVII THE WEEKS WEAR BY Rilla read her first love letter in her Rainbow Valley fir-shadowed nook , and a girl 's first love letter , whatever blase , old people may think of it , be an event of tremendous importance in the teen .
After Kenneth 's regiment have leave Kingsport there come a fortnight of dully-aching anxiety and when the congregation sang in Church on Sunday evening , `` Oh , hear u when we cry to Thee For those in peril on the sea , '' Rilla 's voice always fail her ; for with the word come a horribly vivid mind picture of a submarined ship sink beneath pitiless wave amid the struggle and cry of drown men .
Then word come that Kenneth 's regiment have arrive safely in England ; and now , at last , here be his letter .
It begin with something that make Rilla supremely happy for the moment and end with a paragraph that crimson her cheek with the wonder and thrill and delight of it .
Between begin and end the letter be just such a jolly , newsy epistle a Ken might have write to anyone ; but for the sake of that beginning and end Rilla slept with the letter under her pillow for week , sometimes wake in the night to slip her finger under and just touch it , and look with secret pity on other girl whose sweetheart could never have write them anything half so wonderful and exquisite .
Kenneth be not the son of a famous novelist for nothing .
He `` have a way '' of express thing in a few poignant , significant word that seem to suggest far more than they utter , and never grow stale or flat or foolish with ever so many score of reading .
Rilla go home from Rainbow Valley a if she fly rather than walk .
But such moment of uplift be rare that autumn .
To be sure , there be one day in September when great news come of a big Allied victory in the west and Susan run out to hoist the flag -- the first time she have hoist it since the Russian line break and the last time she be to hoist it for many dismal moon .
`` Likely the Big Push have begin at last , Mrs. Dr. dear , '' she exclaim , `` and we will soon see the finish of the Huns .
Our boy will be home by Christmas now .
Hurrah ! ''
Susan be ashamed of herself for hurrah the minute she have do it , and apologize meekly for such an outburst of juvenility .
`` But indeed , Mrs. Dr. dear , this good news have go to my head after this awful summer of Russian slump and Gallipoli setback . ''
`` Good news ! ''
say Miss Oliver bitterly .
`` I wonder if the woman whose men have be kill for it will call it good news .
Just because our own men be not on that part of the front we be rejoice a if the victory have cost no life . ''
`` Now , Miss Oliver dear , do not take that view of it , '' deprecate Susan .
`` We have not have much to rejoice over of late and yet men be be kill just the same .
Do not let yourself slump like poor Cousin Sophia .
She say , when the word come , ` Ah , it be nothing but a rift in the cloud .
We be up this week but we will be down the next . '
` Well , Sophia Crawford , ' say I , -- for I will never give in to her , Mrs. Dr. dear -- ` God himself can not make two hill without a hollow between them , a I have hear it say , but that be no reason why we should not take the good of the hill when we be on them . '
But Cousin Sophia moan on .
` Here be the Gallipolly expedition a failure and the Grand Duke Nicholas send off , and everyone know the Czar of Rooshia be a pro-German and the Allies have no ammunition and Bulgaria be go against u .
And the end be not yet , for England and France must be punish for their deadly sin until they repent in sackcloth and ash . ' '
I think myself , ' I say , ` that they will do their repenting in khaki and trench mud , and it seem to me that the Huns should have a few sin to repent of also . '
` They be instrument in the hand of the Almighty , to purge the garner , ' say Sophia .
And then I get mad , Mrs. Dr. dear , and tell her I do not and never would believe that the Almighty ever take such dirty instrument in hand for any purpose whatever , and that I do not consider it decent for her to be use the word of Holy Writ as glibly a she be do in ordinary conversation .
She be not , I tell her , a minister or even an elder .
And for the time be I squelch her , Mrs. Dr. dear .
Cousin Sophia have no spirit .
She be very different from her niece , Mrs. Dean Crawford over-harbour .
You know the Dean Crawfords have five boy and now the new baby be another boy .
All the connection and especially Dean Crawford be much disappoint because their heart have be set on a girl ; but Mrs. Dean just laugh and say , ` Everywhere I go this summer I saw the sign `` MEN WANTED '' star me in the face .
Do you think I could go and have a girl under such circumstance ? '
There be spirit for you , Mrs. Dr. dear .
But Cousin Sophia would say the child be just so much more cannon fodder . ''
Cousin Sophia have full range for her pessimism that gloomy autumn , and even Susan , incorrigible old optimist a she be , be hard put to it for cheer .
When Bulgaria line up with Germany Susan only remark scornfully , `` One more nation anxious for a licking , '' but the Greek tangle worry her beyond her power of philosophy to endure calmly .
`` Constantine of Greece have a German wife , Mrs. Dr. dear , and that fact squelch hope .
To think that I should have live to care what kind of a wife Constantine of Greece have !
The miserable creature be under his wife 's thumb and that be a bad place for any man to be .
I be an old maid and an old maid have to be independent or she will be squash out .
But if I have be a married woman , Mrs. Dr. dear , I would have be meek and humble .
It be my opinion that this Sophia of Greece be a minx . ''
Susan be furious when the news come that Venizelos have meet with defeat .
`` I could spank Constantine and skin him alive afterwards , that I could , '' she exclaim bitterly .
`` Oh , Susan , I 'm surprised at you , '' say the doctor , pull a long face .
`` Have you no regard for the propriety ?
Skin him alive by all mean but omit the spanking . ''
`` If he have be well spank in his younger day he might have more sense now , '' retort Susan .
`` But I suppose prince be never spank , more be the pity .
I see the Allies have send him an ultimatum .
I could tell them that it will take more than ultimatum to skin a snake like Constantine .
Perhaps the Allied blockade will hammer sense into his head ; but that will take some time I be think , and in the meantime what be to become of poor Serbia ? ''
They saw what become of Serbia , and during the process Susan be hardly to be live with .
In her exasperation she abuse everything and everybody except Kitchener , and she fell upon poor President Wilson tooth and claw .
`` If he have do his duty and go into the war long ago we should not have see this mess in Serbia , '' she avow .
`` It would be a serious thing to plunge a great country like the United States , with it mixed population , into the war , Susan , '' say the doctor , who sometimes come to the defence of the President , not because he think Wilson need it especially , but from an unholy love of bait Susan .
`` Maybe , doctor dear -- maybe !
But that make me think of the old story of the girl who tell her grandmother she be go to be marry .
` It be a solemn thing to be marry , ' say the old lady .
` Yes , but it be a solemn thing not to be , ' say the girl .
And I can testify to that out of my own experience , doctor dear .
And I think it be a solemn thing for the Yankees that they have keep out of the war than it would have be if they have go into it .
However , though I do not know much about them , I be of the opinion that we will see them start something yet , Woodrow Wilson or no Woodrow Wilson , when they get it into their head that this war be not a correspondence school .
They will not , '' say Susan , energetically wave a saucepan with one hand and a soup ladle with the other , `` be too proud to fight then . ''
On a pale-yellow , windy evening in October Carl Meredith go away .
He have enlist on his eighteenth birthday .
John Meredith saw him off with a set face .
His two boy be go -- there be only little Bruce leave now .
He love Bruce and Bruce 's mother dearly ; but Jerry and Carl be the son of the bride of his youth and Carl be the only one of all his child who have Cecilia 's very eye .
As they look lovingly out at him above Carl 's uniform the pale minister suddenly remember the day when for the first and last time he have try to whip Carl for his prank with the eel .
That be the first time he have realise how much Carl 's eye be like Cecilia 's .
Now he realise it again once more .
Would he ever again see his dead wife 's eye look at him from his son 's face ?
What a bonny , clean , handsome lad he be !
It be -- hard -- to see him go .
John Meredith seem to be look at a torn plain strew with the body of `` able-bodied men between the age of eighteen and forty-five . ''
Only the other day Carl have be a little scrap of a boy , hunt bug in Rainbow Valley , take lizard to bed with him , and scandalize the Glen by carry frog to Sunday School .
It seem hardly -- right -- somehow that he should be an `` able-bodied man '' in khaki .
Yet John Meredith have say no word to dissuade him when Carl have tell him he must go .
Rilla felt Carl 's go keenly .
They have always be crony and playmate .
He be only a little old than she be and they have be child in Rainbow Valley together .
She recall all their old prank and escapade a she walk slowly home alone .
The full moon peep through the scudding cloud with sudden flood of weird illumination , the telephone wire sing a shrill weird song in the wind , and the tall spike of withered , grey-headed golden-rod in the fence corner sway and beckon wildly to her like group of old witch weave unholy spell .
On such a night a this , long ago , Carl would come over to Ingleside and whistle her out to the gate .
`` Let 's go on a moon-spree , Rilla , '' he would say , and the two of them would scamper off to Rainbow Valley .
Rilla have never be afraid of his beetle and bug , though she draw a hard and fast line at snake .
They use to talk together of almost everything and be tease about each other at school ; but one evening when they be about ten year of age they have solemnly promise , by the old spring in Rainbow Valley , that they would never marry each other .
Alice Clow have `` cross out '' their name on her slate in school that day , and it come out that `` both married . ''
They do not like the idea at all , hence the mutual vow in Rainbow Valley .
There be nothing like an ounce of prevention .
Rilla laugh over the old memory -- and then sigh .
That very day a dispatch from some London paper have contain the cheerful announcement that `` the present moment be the darkest since the war begin . ''
It be dark enough , and Rilla wish desperately that she could do something besides wait and serve at home , a day after day the Glen boys she have know go away .
If she be only a boy , speed in khaki by Carl 's side to the Western front !
She have wish that in a burst of romance when Jem have go , without , perhaps , really mean it .
She mean it now .
There be moment when wait at home , in safety and comfort , seem an unendurable thing .
The moon burst triumphantly through an especially dark cloud and shadow and silver chase each other in wave over the Glen .
Rilla remember one moonlit evening of childhood when she have say to her mother , `` The moon just look like a sorry , sorry face . ''
She think it look like that still -- an agonised , care-worn face , a though it look down on dreadful sight .
What do it see on the Western front ?
In break Serbia ?
On shell-swept Gallipoli ?
`` I be tired , '' Miss Oliver have say that day , in a rare outburst of impatience , `` of this horrible rack of strained emotion , when every day bring a new horror or the dread of it .
No , do n't look reproachfully at me , Mrs. Blythe .
There 's nothing heroic about me today .
I 've slump .
I wish England have leave Belgium to her fate -- I wish Canada have never send a man -- I wish we 'd tie our boy to our apron string and not let one of them go .
Oh -- I shall be ashamed of myself in half an hour -- but at this very minute I mean every word of it .
Will the Allies never strike ? ''
`` Patience be a tired mare but she jog on , '' say Susan .
`` While the steed of Armageddon thunder , trample over our heart , '' retort Miss Oliver .
`` Susan , tell me -- do n't you ever -- do n't you ever -- take spell of feeling that you must scream -- or swear -- or smash something -- just because your torture reach a point when it become unbearable ? ''
`` I have never swear or desire to swear , Miss Oliver dear , but I will admit , '' say Susan , with the air of one determine to make a clean breast of it once and for all , `` that I have experience occasion when it be a relief to do considerable banging . ''
`` Do n't you think that be a kind of swearing , Susan ?
What be the difference between slam a door viciously and say d -- '' `` Miss Oliver dear , '' interrupt Susan , desperately determine to save Gertrude from herself , if human power could do it , `` you be all tire out and unstrung -- and no wonder , teach those obstreperous youngster all day and come home to bad war news .
But just you go upstairs and lie down and I will bring you up a cup of hot tea and a bite of toast and very soon you will not want to slam door or swear . ''
`` Susan , you 're a good soul -- a very pearl of Susans !
But , Susan , it would be such a relief -- to say just one soft , low , little tiny d -- '' `` I will bring you a hot-water bottle for the sol of your foot , also , '' interpose Susan resolutely , `` and it would not be any relief to say that word you be think of , Miss Oliver , and that you may tie to . ''
`` Well , I 'll try the hot-water bottle first , '' say Miss Oliver , repent herself on tease Susan and vanish upstairs , to Susan 's intense relief .
Susan shake her head ominously a she fill the hot-water bottle .
The war be certainly relax the standard of behaviour woefully .
Here be Miss Oliver admittedly on the point of profanity .
`` We must draw the blood from her brain , '' say Susan , `` and if this bottle be not effective I will see what can be do with a mustard plaster . ''
Gertrude rally and carry on .
Lord Kitchener go to Greece , whereat Susan foretell that Constantine would soon experience a change of heart .
Lloyd George begin to heckle the Allies regard equipment and gun and Susan say you would hear more of Lloyd George yet .
The gallant Anzacs withdrew from Gallipoli and Susan approve the step , with reservation .
The siege of Kut-El-Amara begin and Susan pore over map of Mesopotamia and abuse the Turks .
Henry Ford start for Europe and Susan flay him with sarcasm .
Sir John French be supersede by Sir Douglas Haig and Susan dubiously opine that it be poor policy to swap horse cross a stream , `` though , to be sure , Haig be a good name and French have a foreign sound , say what you might . ''
Not a move on the great chess-board of king or bishop or pawn escape Susan , who have once read only Glen St. Mary note .
`` There be a time , '' she say sorrowfully , `` when I do not care what happen outside of P.E . Island , and now a king can not have a toothache in Russia or China but it worry me .
It may be broaden to the mind , a the doctor say , but it be very painful to the feeling . ''
When Christmas come again Susan do not set any vacant place at the festive board .
Two empty chair be too much even for Susan who have think in September that there would not be one .
`` This be the first Christmas that Walter be not home , '' Rilla write in her diary that night .
`` Jem use to be away for Christmases up in Avonlea , but Walter never be .
I have letter from Ken and him today .
They be still in England but expect to be in the trench very soon .
And then -- but I suppose we 'll be able to endure it somehow .
To me , the strange of all the strange thing since 1914 be how we have all learn to accept thing we never think we could -- to go on with life a a matter of course .
I know that Jem and Jerry be in the trench -- that Ken and Walter will be soon -- that if one of them do not come back my heart will break -- yet I go on and work and plan -- yes , and even enjoy life by time .
There be moment when we have real fun because , just for the moment , we do n't think about thing and then -- we remember -- and the remembering be bad than thinking of it all the time would have be .
`` Today be dark and cloudy and tonight be wild enough , a Gertrude say , to please any novelist in search of suitable matter for a murder or elopement .
The raindrop stream over the pane look like tear run down a face , and the wind be shriek through the maple grove .
`` This have n't be a nice Christmas Day in any way .
Nan have toothache and Susan have red eye , and assume a weird and gruesome flippancy of manner to deceive u into think she have n't ; and Jims have a bad cold all day and I 'm afraid of croup .
He have have croup twice since October .
The first time I be nearly frighten to death , for father and mother be both away -- father always be away , it seem to me , when any of this household get sick .
But Susan be cool a a fish and know just what to do , and by morning Jims be all right .
That child be a cross between a duck and an imp .
He 's a year and four month old , trot about everywhere , and say quite a few word .
He have the cut little way of call me `` Willa-will . ''
It always bring back that dreadful , ridiculous , delightful night when Ken come to say good-bye , and I be so furious and happy .
Jims be pink and white and big-eyed and curly-haired and every now and then I discover a new dimple in him .
I can never quite believe he be really the same creature a that scrawny , yellow , ugly little changeling I bring home in the soup tureen .
Nobody have ever hear a word from Jim Anderson .
If he never come back I shall keep Jims always .
Everybody here worship and spoil him -- or would spoil him if Morgan and I do n't stand remorselessly in the way .
Susan say Jims be the cleverest child she ever saw and can recognize Old Nick when he see him -- this because Jims throw poor Doc out of an upstairs window one day .
Doc turn into Mr. Hyde on his way down and land in a currant bush , spit and swearing .
I try to console his inner cat with a saucer of milk but he would have none of it , and remain Mr. Hyde the rest of the day .
Jims 's late exploit be to paint the cushion of the big arm-chair in the sun parlour with molasses ; and before anybody find it out Mrs. Fred Clow come in on Red Cross business and sit down on it .
Her new silk dress be ruin and nobody could blame her for be vex .
But she go into one of her temper and say nasty thing and give me such slam about ` spoil ' Jims that I nearly boil over , too .
But I keep the lid on till she have waddle away and then I explode . ''
` The fat , clumsy , horrid old thing , ' I say -- and oh , what a satisfaction it be to say it . ''
` She have three son at the front , ' mother say rebukingly . '' '
I suppose that cover all her shortcoming in manner , ' I retort .
But I be ashamed -- for it be true that all her boy have go and she be very plucky and loyal about it too ; and she be a perfect tower of strength in the Red Cross .
It 's a little hard to remember all the heroine .
Just the same , it be her second new silk dress in one year and that when everybody be -- or should be -- try to ` save and serve . '
`` I have to bring out my green velvet hat again lately and begin wear it .
I hang on to my blue straw sailor as long a I could .
How I hate the green velvet hat !
It be so elaborate and conspicuous .
I do n't see how I could ever have like it .
But I vow to wear it and wear it I will .
`` Shirley and I go down to the station this morning to take Little Dog Monday a bang-up Christmas dinner .
Dog Monday wait and watch there still , with just a much hope and confidence a ever .
Sometimes he hang around the station house and talk to people and the rest of his time he sit at his little kennel door and watch the track unwinkingly .
We never try to coax him home now : we know it be of no use .
When Jem come back , Monday will come home with him ; and if Jem -- never come back -- Monday will wait there for him as long a his dear dog heart go on beating .
`` Fred Arnold be here last night .
He be eighteen in November and be go to enlist just as soon a his mother be over an operation she have to have .
He have be come here very often lately and though I like him so much it make me uncomfortable , because I be afraid he be think that perhaps I could care something for him .
I ca n't tell him about Ken -- because , after all , what be there to tell ?
And yet I do n't like to behave coldly and distantly when he will be go away so soon .
It be very perplexing .
I remember I use to think it would be such fun to have dozen of beau -- and now I 'm worried to death because two be too many .
`` I be learn to cook .
Susan be teach me .
I try to learn long ago -- but no , let me be honest -- Susan try to teach me , which be a very different thing .
I never seem to succeed with anything and I get discourage .
But since the boy have go away I want to be able to make cake and thing for them myself and so I start in again and this time I 'm get on surprisingly well .
Susan say it be all in the way I hold my mouth and father say my subconscious mind be desirous of learn now , and I dare say they 're both right .
Anyhow , I can make dandy short-bread and fruitcake .
I get ambitious last week and attempted cream puff , but make an awful failure of them .
They come out of the oven flat a fluke .
I think maybe the cream would fill them up again and make them plump but it do n't .
I think Susan be secretly pleased .
She be past mistress in the art of make cream puff and it would break her heart if anyone else here could make them as well .
I wonder if Susan tamper -- but no , I wo n't suspect her of such a thing .
`` Miranda Pryor spend an afternoon here a few day ago , help me cut out certain Red Cross garment know by the charm name of ` vermin shirt . '
Susan think that name be not quite decent , so I suggest she call them ` cootie sarks , ' which be old Highland Sandy 's version of it .
But she shake her head and I hear her tell mother later that , in her opinion , ` cootie ' and ` sarks ' be not proper subject for young girl to talk about .
She be especially horrify when Jem write in his last letter to mother , ` Tell Susan I have a fine cootie hunt this morning and catch fifty-three ! '
Susan positively turn pea-green .
` Mrs. Dr. dear , ' she say , ` when I be young , if decent people be so unfortunate a to get -- those insect -- they keep it a secret if possible .
I do not want to be narrow-minded , Mrs. Dr. dear , but I still think it be well not to mention such thing . '
`` Miranda grow confidential over our vermin shirt and tell me all her trouble .
She be desperately unhappy .
She be engage to Joe Milgrave and Joe join up in October and have be train in Charlottetown ever since .
Her father be furious when he join and forbid Miranda ever to have any dealing or communication with him again .
Poor Joe expect to go overseas any day and want Miranda to marry him before he go , which show that there have be ` communication ' in spite of Whiskers-on-the-moon .
Miranda want to marry him but can not , and she declare it will break her heart . ''
` Why do n't you run away and marry him ? '
I say .
It do n't go against my conscience in the least to give her such advice .
Joe Milgrave be a splendid fellow and Mr. Pryor fairly beam on him until the war break out and I know Mr. Pryor would forgive Miranda very quickly , once it be over and he want his housekeeper back .
But Miranda shake her silvery head dolefully . ''
` Joe want me to but I ca n't .
Mother 's last word to me , a she lay on her dying-bed , be , `` Never , never run away , Miranda , '' and I promise . '
`` Miranda 's mother die two year ago , and it seem , accord to Miranda , that her mother and father actually run away to be marry themselves .
To picture Whiskers-on-the-moon a the hero of an elopement be beyond my power .
But such be the case and Mrs. Pryor at least lived to repent it .
She have a hard life of it with Mr. Pryor , and she think it be a punishment on her for run away .
So she make Miranda promise she would never , for any reason whatever , do it .
`` Of course , you can not urge a girl to break a promise make to a die mother , so I do not see what Miranda could do unless she get Joe to come to the house when her father be away and marry her there .
But Miranda say that could n't be manage .
Her father seem to suspect she might be up to something of the sort and he never go away for long at a time , and , of course , Joe could n't get leave of absence at an hour 's notice . ''
` No , I shall just have to let Joe go , and he will be kill -- I know he will be kill -- and my heart will break , ' say Miranda , her tear run down and copiously bedew the vermin shirt !
`` I be not write like this for lack of any real sympathy with poor Miranda .
I 've just get into the habit of give thing a comical twist if I can , when I 'm write to Jem and Walter and Ken , to make them laugh .
I really felt sorry for Miranda who be as much in love with Joe a a china-blue girl can be with anyone and who be dreadfully ashamed of her father 's pro-German sentiment .
I think she understand that I do , for she say she have want to tell me all about her worry because I have grow so sympathetic this past year .
I wonder if I have .
I know I use to be a selfish , thoughtless creature -- how selfish and thoughtless I be ashamed to remember now , so I ca n't be quite so bad a I be .
`` I wish I could help Miranda .
It would be very romantic to contrive a war-wedding and I should dearly love to get the good of Whiskers-on-the-moon .
But at present the oracle have not speak . ''
CHAPTER XVIII A WAR-WEDDING `` I can tell you this Dr. dear , '' say Susan , pale with wrath , `` that Germany be get to be perfectly ridiculous . ''
They be all in the big Ingleside kitchen .
Susan be mix biscuit for supper .
Mrs. Blythe be make shortbread for Jem , and Rilla be compound candy for Ken and Walter -- it have once be `` Walter and Ken '' in her thought but somehow , quite unconsciously , this have change until Ken 's name come naturally first .
Cousin Sophia be also there , knit .
All the boy be go to be kill in the long run , so Cousin Sophia felt in her bone , but they might better die with warm foot than cold one , so Cousin Sophia knit faithfully and gloomily .
Into this peaceful scene erupt the doctor , wrathful and excite over the burning of the Parliament Buildings in Ottawa .
And Susan become automatically quite a wrathful and excited .
`` What will those Huns do next ? ''
she demand .
`` Coming over here and burn our Parliament building !
Did anyone ever hear of such an outrage ? ''
`` We do n't know that the Germans be responsible for this , '' say the doctor -- much a if he felt quite sure they be .
`` Fires do start without their agency sometimes .
And Uncle Mark MacAllister 's barn be burn last week .
You can hardly accuse the Germans of that , Susan . ''
`` Indeed , Dr. dear , I do not know . ''
Susan nod slowly and portentously .
`` Whiskers-on-the-moon be there that very day .
The fire break out half an hour after he be go .
So much be a fact -- but I shall not accuse a Presbyterian elder of burn anybody 's barn until I have proof .
However , everybody know , Dr. dear , that both Uncle Mark 's boy have enlist , and that Uncle Mark himself make speech at all the recruiting meeting .
So no doubt Germany be anxious to get square with him . ''
`` I could never speak at a recruiting meeting , '' say Cousin Sophia solemnly .
`` I could never reconcile it to my conscience to ask another woman 's son to go , to murder and be murder . ''
`` Could you not ? ''
say Susan .
`` Well , Sophia Crawford , I felt a if I could ask anyone to go when I read last night that there be no child under eight year of age leave alive in Poland .
Think of that , Sophia Crawford '' -- Susan shake a floury finger at Sophia -- `` not -- one -- child -- under -- eight -- year -- of -- age ! ''
`` I suppose the Germans have et 'em all , '' sigh Cousin Sophia .
`` Well , no-o-o , '' say Susan reluctantly , a if she hat to admit that there be any crime the Huns could n't be accuse of .
`` The Germans have not turn cannibal yet -- as far a I know .
They have die of starvation and exposure , the poor little creature .
There be murder for you , Cousin Sophia Crawford .
The thought of it poison every bite and sup I take . ''
`` I see that Fred Carson of Lowbridge have be award a Distinguished Conduct Medal , '' remark the doctor , over his local paper .
`` I hear that last week , '' say Susan .
`` He be a battalion runner and he do something extra brave and dare .
His letter , tell his folk about it , come when his old Grandmother Carson be on her dying-bed .
She have only a few minute more to live and the Episcopal minister , who be there , ask her if she would not like him to pray .
` Oh yes , yes , you can pray , ' she say impatient-like -- she be a Dean , Dr. dear , and the Deans be always high-spirited -- ` you can pray , but for pity 's sake pray low and do n't disturb me .
I want to think over this splendid news and I have not much time leave to do it . '
That be Almira Carson all over .
Fred be the apple of her eye .
She be seventy-five year of age and have not a grey hair in her head , they tell me . ''
`` By the way , that remind me -- I find a grey hair this morning -- my very first , '' say Mrs. Blythe .
`` I have notice that grey hair for some time , Mrs. Dr. dear , but I do not speak of it .
Thought I to myself , ` She have enough to bear . '
But now that you have discover it let me remind you that grey hair be honourable . ''
`` I must be get old , Gilbert . ''
Mrs. Blythe laugh a trifle ruefully .
`` People be begin to tell me I look so young .
They never tell you that when you be young .
But I shall not worry over my silver thread .
I never like red hair .
Gilbert , do I ever tell you of that time , year ago at Green Gables , when I dye my hair ?
Nobody but Marilla and I know about it . ''
`` Was that the reason you come out once with your hair shingle to the bone ? ''
`` Yes .
I buy a bottle of dye from a German Jew pedlar .
I fondly expect it would turn my hair black -- and it turn it green .
So it have to be cut off . ''
`` You have a narrow escape , Mrs. Dr. dear , '' exclaim Susan .
`` Of course you be too young then to know what a German be .
It be a special mercy of Providence that it be only green dye and not poison . ''
`` It seem hundred of year since those Green Gables day , '' sigh Mrs. Blythe .
`` They belong to another world altogether .
Life have be cut in two by the chasm of war .
What be ahead I do n't know -- but it ca n't be a bit like the past .
I wonder if those of u who have live half our life in the old world will ever feel wholly at home in the new . ''
`` Have you notice , '' ask Miss Oliver , glance up from her book , `` how everything write before the war seem so far away now , too ?
One feel a if one be read something as ancient a the Iliad .
This poem of Wordsworth 's -- the Senior class have it in their entrance work -- I 've be glance over it .
Its classic calm and repose and the beauty of the line seem to belong to another planet , and to have as little to do with the present world-welter a the evening star . ''
`` The only thing that I find much comfort in reading nowadays be the Bible , '' remark Susan , whisk her biscuit into the oven .
`` There be so many passage in it that seem to me exactly descriptive of the Huns .
Old Highland Sandy declare that there be no doubt that the Kaiser be the Anti-Christ spoken of in Revelations , but I do not go as far a that .
It would , in my humble opinion , Mrs. Dr. dear , be too great an honour for him . ''
Early one morning , several day later , Miranda Pryor slip up to Ingleside , ostensibly to get some Red Cross sewing , but in reality to talk over with sympathetic Rilla trouble that be past bearing alone .
She bring her dog with her -- an over-fed , bandy-legged little animal very dear to her heart because Joe Milgrave have give it to her when it be a puppy .
Mr. Pryor regard all dog with disfavour ; but in those day he have look kindly upon Joe a a suitor for Miranda 's hand and so he have allow her to keep the puppy .
Miranda be so grateful that she endeavour to please her father by name her dog after his political idol , the great Liberal chieftain , Sir Wilfrid Laurier -- though his title be soon abbreviate to Wilfy .
Sir Wilfrid grow and flourish and waxed fat ; but Miranda spoil him absurdly and nobody else like him .
Rilla especially hat him because of his detestable trick of lie flat on his back and entreating you with wave paw to tickle his sleek stomach .
When she saw that Miranda 's pale eye bore unmistakable testimony of her have cry all night , Rilla ask her to come up to her room , know Miranda have a tale of woe to tell , but she order Sir Wilfrid to remain below .
`` Oh , ca n't he come , too ? ''
say Miranda wistfully .
`` Poor Wilfy wo n't be any bother -- and I wipe his paw so carefully before I bring him in .
He be always so lonesome in a strange place without me -- and very soon he 'll be -- all -- I 'll have leave -- to remind me -- of Joe . ''
Rilla yield , and Sir Wilfrid , with his tail curl at a saucy angle over his brindled back , trot triumphantly up the stair before them .
`` Oh , Rilla , '' sob Miranda , when they have reach sanctuary .
`` I 'm so unhappy .
I ca n't begin to tell you how unhappy I be .
Truly , my heart be break . ''
Rilla sit down on the lounge beside her .
Sir Wilfrid squat on his haunch before them , with his impertinent pink tongue stick out , and listen .
`` What be the trouble , Miranda ? ''
`` Joe be come home tonight on his last leave .
I have a letter from him on Saturday -- he send my letter in care of Bob Crawford , you know , because of father -- and , oh , Rilla , he will only have four day -- he have to go away Friday morning -- and I may never see him again . ''
`` Does he still want you to marry him ? ''
ask Rilla .
`` Oh , yes .
He implore me in his letter to run away and be marry .
But I can not do that , Rilla , not even for Joe .
My only comfort be that I will be able to see him for a little while tomorrow afternoon .
Father have to go to Charlottetown on business .
At least we will have one good farewell talk .
But oh -- afterwards -- why , Rilla , I know father wo n't even let me go to the station Friday morning to see Joe off . ''
`` Why in the world do n't you and Joe get marry tomorrow afternoon at home ? ''
demand Rilla .
Miranda swallow a sob in such amazement that she almost choke .
`` Why -- why -- that be impossible , Rilla . ''
`` Why ? ''
briefly demand the organizer of the Junior Red Cross and the transporter of baby in soup tureen .
`` Why -- why -- we never think of such a thing -- Joe have n't a license -- I have no dress -- I could n't be marry in black -- I -- I -- we -- you -- you -- '' Miranda lose herself altogether and Sir Wilfrid , see that she be in dire distress throw back his head and emit a melancholy yelp .
Rilla Blythe think hard and rapidly for a few minute .
Then she say , `` Miranda , if you will put yourself into my hand I 'll have you marry to Joe before four o'clock tomorrow afternoon . ''
`` Oh , you could n't . ''
`` I can and I will .
But you 'll have to do exactly a I tell you . ''
`` Oh -- I -- do n't think -- oh , father will kill me -- '' `` Nonsense .
He 'll be very angry I suppose .
But be you more afraid of your father 's anger than you be of Joe 's never come back to you ? ''
`` No , '' say Miranda , with sudden firmness , `` I 'm not . ''
`` Will you do a I tell you then ? ''
`` Yes , I will . ''
`` Then get Joe on the long-distance at once and tell him to bring out a license and ring tonight . ''
`` Oh , I could n't , '' wail the aghast Miranda , `` it -- it would be so -- so indelicate . ''
Rilla shut her little white teeth together with a snap .
`` Heaven grant me patience , '' she say under her breath .
`` I 'll do it then , '' she say aloud , `` and meanwhile , you go home and make what preparation you can .
When I ` phone down to you to come up and help me sew come at once . ''
As soon a Miranda , pallid , scar , but desperately resolve , have go , Rilla fly to the telephone and put in a long-distance call for Charlottetown .
She get through with such surprising quickness that she be convinced Providence approve of her undertaking , but it be a good hour before she could get in touch with Joe Milgrave at his camp .
Meanwhile , she pace impatiently about , and pray that when she do get Joe there would be no listener on the line to carry news to Whiskers-on-the-moon .
`` Is that you , Joe ?
Rilla Blythe be speak -- Rilla -- Rilla -- oh , never mind .
Listen to this .
Before you come home tonight get a marriage license -- a marriage license -- yes , a marriage license -- and a wedding-ring .
Did you get that ?
And will you do it ?
Very well , be sure you do it -- it be your only chance . ''
Flushed with triumph -- for her only fear be that she might not be able to locate Joe in time -- Rilla ring the Pryor ring .
This time she have not such good luck for she draw Whiskers-on-the-moon .
`` Is that Miranda ?
Oh -- Mr. Pryor !
Well , Mr. Pryor , will you kindly ask Miranda if she can come up this afternoon and help me with some sewing .
It be very important , or I would not trouble her .
Oh -- thank you . ''
Mr. Pryor have consent somewhat grumpily , but he have consent -- he do not want to offend Dr. Blythe , and he know that if he refuse to allow Miranda to do any Red Cross work public opinion would make the Glen too hot for comfort .
Rilla go out to the kitchen , shut all the door with a mysterious expression which alarm Susan , and then say solemnly , `` Susan can you make a wedding-cake this afternoon ? ''
`` A wedding-cake ! ''
Susan star .
Rilla have , without any warning , bring her a war-baby once upon a time .
Was she now , with equal suddenness , go to produce a husband ?
`` Yes , a wedding-cake -- a scrumptious wedding-cake , Susan -- a beautiful , plummy , eggy , citron-peely wedding-cake .
And we must make other thing too .
I 'll help you in the morning .
But I ca n't help you in the afternoon for I have to make a wedding-dress and time be the essence of the contract , Susan . ''
Susan felt that she be really too old to be subject to such shock .
`` Who be you go to marry , Rilla ? ''
she ask feebly .
`` Susan , darling , I be not the happy bride .
Miranda Pryor be go to marry Joe Milgrave tomorrow afternoon while her father be away in town .
A war-wedding , Susan -- be n't that thrill and romantic ?
I never be so excited in my life . ''
The excitement soon spread over Ingleside , infect even Mrs. Blythe and Susan .
`` I 'll go to work on that cake at once , '' vow Susan , with a glance at the clock .
`` Mrs. Dr. dear , will you pick over the fruit and beat up the egg ?
If you will I can have that cake ready for the oven by the evening .
Tomorrow morning we can make salad and other thing .
I will work all night if necessary to get the good of Whiskers-on-the-moon . ''
Miranda arrive , tearful and breathless .
`` We must fix over my white dress for you to wear , '' say Rilla .
`` It will fit you very nicely with a little alteration . ''
To work go the two girl , rip , fitting , basting , sew for dear life .
By dint of unceasing effort they get the dress do by seven o'clock and Miranda try it on in Rilla 's room .
`` It 's very pretty -- but oh , if I could just have a veil , '' sigh Miranda .
`` I 've always dream of be marry in a lovely white veil . ''
Some good fairy evidently wait on the wish of war-brides .
The door open and Mrs. Blythe come in , her arm full of a filmy burden .
`` Miranda dear , '' she say , `` I want you to wear my wedding-veil tomorrow .
It be twenty-four year since I be a bride at old Green Gables -- the happy bride that ever be -- and the wedding-veil of a happy bride bring good luck , they say . ''
`` Oh , how sweet of you , Mrs. Blythe , '' say Miranda , the ready tear start to her eye .
The veil be try on and drape .
Susan drop in to approve but dare not linger .
`` I 've get that cake in the oven , '' she say , `` and I be pursue a policy of watchful waiting .
The evening news be that the Grand Duke have capture Erzerum .
That be a pill for the Turks .
I wish I have a chance to tell the Czar just what a mistake he make when he turn Nicholas down . ''
Susan disappear downstairs to the kitchen , whence a dreadful thud and a piercing shriek presently sound .
Everybody rush to the kitchen -- the doctor and Miss Oliver , Mrs. Blythe , Rilla , Miranda in her wedding-veil .
Susan be sit flatly in the middle of the kitchen floor with a daze , bewilder look on her face , while Doc , evidently in his Hyde incarnation , be stand on the dresser , with his back up , his eye blazing , and his tail the size of three tail .
`` Susan , what have happen ? ''
cried Mrs. Blythe in alarm .
`` Did you fall ?
Are you hurt ? ''
Susan pick herself up .
`` No , '' she say grimly , `` I be not hurt , though I be jar all over .
Do not be alarm .
As for what have happen -- I try to kick that darn cat with both foot , that be what happen . ''
Everybody shriek with laughter .
The doctor be quite helpless .
`` Oh , Susan , Susan , '' he gasp .
`` That I should live to hear you swear . ''
`` I be sorry , '' say Susan in real distress , `` that I use such an expression before two young girl .
But I say that beast be darn , and darn it be .
It belong to Old Nick . ''
`` Do you expect it will vanish some of these day with a bang and the odour of brimstone , Susan ? ''
`` It will go to it own place in due time and that you may tie to , '' say Susan dourly , shake out her raddled bone and go to her oven .
`` I suppose my plunk down like that have shake my cake so that it will be as heavy a lead . ''
But the cake be not heavy .
It be all a bride 's cake should be , and Susan ice it beautifully .
Next day she and Rilla work all the forenoon , make delicacy for the wedding-feast , and as soon a Miranda phone up that her father be safely off everything be pack in a big hamper and take down to the Pryor house .
Joe soon arrive in his uniform and a state of violent excitement , accompany by his best man , Sergeant Malcolm Crawford .
There be quite a few guest , for all the Manse and Ingleside folk be there , and a dozen or so of Joe 's relative , include his mother , `` Mrs. Dead Angus Milgrave , '' so call , cheerfully , to distinguish her from another lady whose Angus be live .
Mrs. Dead Angus wear a rather disapprove expression , not care over-much for this alliance with the house of Whiskers-on-the-moon .
So Miranda Pryor be marry to Private Joseph Milgrave on his last leave .
It should have be a romantic wedding but it be not .
There be too many factor work against romance , a even Rilla have to admit .
In the first place , Miranda , in spite of her dress and veil , be such a flat-faced , commonplace , uninteresting little bride .
In the second place , Joe cry bitterly all through the ceremony , and this vexed Miranda unreasonably .
Long afterwards she tell Rilla , `` I just felt like say to him then and there , ` If you feel so bad over have to marry me you do n't have to . '
But it be just because he be think all the time of how soon he would have to leave me . ''
In the third place , Jims , who be usually so well-behaved in public , take a fit of shyness and contrariness combine and begin to cry at the top of his voice for `` Willa . ''
Nobody want to take him out , because everybody want to see the marriage , so Rilla who be a bridesmaid , have to take him and hold him during the ceremony .
In the fourth place , Sir Wilfrid Laurier take a fit .
Sir Wilfrid be entrench in a corner of the room behind Miranda 's piano .
During his seizure he make the weird , most unearthly noise .
He would begin with a series of choke , spasmodic sound , continue into a gruesome gurgle , and end up with a strangled howl .
Nobody could hear a word Mr. Meredith be say , except now and then , when Sir Wilfrid stop for breath .
Nobody look at the bride except Susan , who never drag her fascinate eye from Miranda 's face -- all the others be gaze at the dog .
Miranda have be tremble with nervousness but as soon a Sir Wilfrid begin his performance she forget it .
All that she could think of be that her dear dog be die and she could not go to him .
She never remember a word of the ceremony .
Rilla , who in spite of Jims , have be try her best to look rapt and romantic , a beseem a war bridesmaid , give up the hopeless attempt , and devote her energy to choke down untimely merriment .
She dare not look at anybody in the room , especially Mrs. Dead Angus , for fear all her suppressed mirth should suddenly explode in a most un-young-ladylike yell of laughter .
But marry they be , and then they have a wedding-supper in the dining-room which be so lavish and bountiful that you would have think it be the product of a month 's labour .
Everybody have bring something .
Mrs. Dead Angus have bring a large apple-pie , which she place on a chair in the dining-room and then absently sit down on it .
Neither her temper nor her black silk wed garment be improve thereby , but the pie be never miss at the gay bridal feast .
Mrs. Dead Angus eventually take it home with her again .
Whiskers-on-the-moon 's pacifist pig should not get it , anyhow .
That even Mr. and Mrs. Joe , accompany by the recovered Sir Wilfrid , depart for the Four Winds Lighthouse , which be keep by Joe 's uncle and in which they mean to spend their brief honeymoon .
Una Meredith and Rilla and Susan wash the dish , tidy up , leave a cold supper and Miranda 's pitiful little note on the table for Mr. Pryor , and walk home , while the mystic veil of dreamy , haunt winter twilight wrap itself over the Glen .
`` I would really not have mind be a war-bride myself , '' remark Susan sentimentally .
But Rilla felt rather flat -- perhaps a a reaction to all the excitement and rush of the past thirty-six hour .
She be disappointed somehow -- the whole affair have be so ludicrous , and Miranda and Joe so lachrymose and commonplace .
`` If Miranda have n't give that wretched dog such an enormous dinner he would n't have have that fit , '' she say crossly .
`` I warn her -- but she say she could n't starve the poor dog -- he would soon be all she have leave , etc . .
I could have shake her . ''
`` The best man be more excited than Joe be , '' say Susan .
`` He wish Miranda many happy return of the day .
She do not look very happy , but perhaps you could not expect that under the circumstance . ''
`` Anyhow , '' think Rilla , `` I can write a perfectly kill account of it all to the boy .
How Jem will howl over Sir Wilfrid 's part in it ! ''
But if Rilla be rather disappointed in the war wedding she find nothing lack on Friday morning when Miranda say good-bye to her bridegroom at the Glen station .
The dawn be white a a pearl , clear a a diamond .
Behind the station the balsamy copse of young fir be frost-misted .
The cold moon of dawn hung over the westering snow field but the golden fleece of sunrise shone above the maple up at Ingleside .
Joe take his pale little bride in his arm and she lift her face to his .
Rilla choke suddenly .
It do not matter that Miranda be insignificant and commonplace and flat-featured .
It do not matter that she be the daughter of Whiskers-on-the-moon .
All that matter be that rapt , sacrificial look in her eye -- that ever-burning , sacred fire of devotion and loyalty and fine courage that she be mutely promising Joe she and thousand of other woman would keep alive at home while their men hold the Western front .
Rilla walk away , realise that she must not spy on such a moment .
She go down to the end of the platform where Sir Wilfrid and Dog Monday be sit , look at each other .
Sir Wilfrid remark condescendingly : `` Why do you haunt this old shed when you might lie on the hearthrug at Ingleside and live on the fat of the land ?
Is it a pose ?
Or a fixed idea ? ''
Whereat Dog Monday , laconically : `` I have a tryst to keep . ''
When the train have go Rilla rejoin the little trembling Miranda .
`` Well , he 's go , '' say Miranda , `` and he may never come back -- but I 'm his wife , and I 'm go to be worthy of him .
I 'm go home . ''
`` Do n't you think you have well come with me now ? ''
ask Rilla doubtfully .
Nobody know yet how Mr. Pryor have take the matter .
`` No .
If Joe can face the Huns I guess I can face father , '' say Miranda daringly .
`` A soldier 's wife ca n't be a coward .
Come on , Wilfy .
I 'll go straight home and meet the bad . ''
There be nothing very dreadful to face , however .
Perhaps Mr. Pryor have reflect that housekeeper be hard to get and that there be many Milgrave home open to Miranda -- also , that there be such a thing a a separation allowance .
At all event , though he tell her grumpily that she have make a nice fool of herself , and would live to regret it , he say nothing worse , and Mrs. Joe put on her apron and go to work as usual , while Sir Wilfrid Laurier , who have a poor opinion of lighthouse for winter residence , go to sleep in his pet nook behind the woodbox , a thankful dog that he be do with war-weddings .
CHAPTER XIX `` THEY SHALL NOT PASS '' One cold grey morning in February Gertrude Oliver waken with a shiver , slip into Rilla 's room , and crept in beside her .
`` Rilla -- I 'm frightened -- frighten a a baby -- I 've have another of my strange dream .
Something terrible be before u -- I know . ''
`` What be it ? ''
ask Rilla .
`` I be stand again on the veranda step -- just a I stand in that dream on the night before the lighthouse dance , and in the sky a huge black , menace thunder cloud roll up from the east .
I could see it shadow racing before it and when it envelop me I shiver with icy cold .
Then the storm break -- and it be a dreadful storm -- blind flash after flash and deafen peal after peal , drive torrent of rain .
I turn in panic and try to run for shelter , and a I do so a man -- a soldier in the uniform of a French army officer -- dash up the step and stand beside me on the threshold of the door .
His clothes be soak with blood from a wound in his breast , he seem spent and exhaust ; but his white face be set and his eye blaze in his hollow face .
` They shall not pass , ' he say , in low , passionate tone which I hear distinctly amid all the turmoil of the storm .
Then I awaken .
Rilla , I 'm frightened -- the spring will not bring the Big Push we 've all be hop for -- instead it be go to bring some dreadful blow to France .
I be sure of it .
The Germans will try to smash through somewhere . ''
`` But he tell you that they would not pass , '' say Rilla , seriously .
She never laugh at Gertrude 's dream a the doctor do .
`` I do not know if that be prophecy or desperation , Rilla , the horror of that dream hold me yet in an icy grip .
We shall need all our courage before long . ''
Dr. Blythe do laugh at the breakfast table -- but he never laugh at Miss Oliver 's dream again ; for that day bring news of the opening of the Verdun offensive , and thereafter through all the beautiful week of spring the Ingleside family , one and all , live in a trance of dread .
There be day when they wait in despair for the end a foot by foot the Germans crept nearer and nearer to the grim barrier of desperate France .
Susan 's deed be in her spotless kitchen at Ingleside , but her thought be on the hill around Verdun .
`` Mrs. Dr. dear , '' she would stick her head in at Mrs. Blythe 's door the last thing at night to remark , `` I do hope the French have hang onto the Crow 's Wood today , '' and she wake at dawn to wonder if Dead Man 's Hill -- surely name by some prophet -- be still hold by the `` poyloos . ''
Susan could have draw a map of the country around Verdun that would have satisfy a chief of staff .
`` If the Germans capture Verdun the spirit of France will be break , '' Miss Oliver say bitterly .
`` But they will not capture it , '' staunchly say Susan , who could not eat her dinner that day for fear l they do that very thing .
`` In the first place , you dream they would not -- you dream the very thing the French be say before they ever say it -- ` they shall not pass . '
I declare to you , Miss Oliver , dear , when I read that in the paper , and remember your dream , I go cold all over with awe .
It seem to me like Biblical time when people dream thing like that quite frequently .
`` I know -- I know , '' say Gertrude , walk restlessly about .
`` I cling to a persistent faith in my dream , too -- but every time bad news come it fail me .
Then I tell myself ` mere coincidence ' -- ` subconscious memory ' and so forth . ''
`` I do not see how any memory could remember a thing before it be ever say at all , '' persist Susan , `` though of course I be not educate like you and the doctor .
I would rather not be , if it make anything as simple a that so hard to believe .
But in any case we need not worry over Verdun , even if the Huns get it .
Joffre say it have no military significance . ''
`` That old sop of comfort have be serve up too often already when revers come , '' retort Gertrude .
`` It have lose it power to charm . ''
`` Was there ever a battle like this in the world before ? ''
say Mr. Meredith , one evening in mid-April .
`` It 's such a titanic thing we ca n't grasp it , '' say the doctor .
`` What be the scrap of a few Homeric handful compare to this ?
The whole Trojan war might be fight around a Verdun fort and a newspaper correspondent would give it no more than a sentence .
I be not in the confidence of the occult power '' -- the doctor throw Gertrude a twinkle -- `` but I have a hunch that the fate of the whole war hang on the issue of Verdun .
As Susan and Joffre say , it have no real military significance ; but it have the tremendous significance of an Idea .
If Germany win there she will win the war .
If she lose , the tide will set against her . ''
`` Lose she will , '' say Mr. Meredith : emphatically .
`` The Idea can not be conquer .
France be certainly very wonderful .
It seem to me that in her I see the white form of civilization make a determined stand against the black power of barbarism .
I think our whole world realize this and that be why we all await the issue so breathlessly .
It be n't merely the question of a few fort change hand or a few mile of blood-soaked ground lose and win . ''
`` I wonder , '' say Gertrude dreamily , `` if some great blessing , great enough for the price , will be the meed of all our pain ?
Is the agony in which the world be shudder the birth-pang of some wondrous new era ?
Or be it merely a futile struggle of ant In the gleam of a million million of sun ?
We think very lightly , Mr. Meredith , of a calamity which destroy an ant-hill and half it inhabitant .
Does the Power that run the universe think u of more importance than we think ant ? ''
`` You forget , '' say Mr. Meredith , with a flash of his dark eye , `` that an infinite Power must be infinitely little as well a infinitely great .
We be neither , therefore there be thing too little as well a too great for u to apprehend .
To the infinitely little an ant be of as much importance a a mastodon .
We be witness the birth-pangs of a new era -- but it will be bear a feeble , wail life like everything else .
I be not one of those who expect a new heaven and a new earth a the immediate result of this war .
That be not the way God work .
But work He do , Miss Oliver , and in the end His purpose will be fulfil . ''
`` Sound and orthodox -- sound and orthodox , '' mutter Susan approvingly in the kitchen .
Susan like to see Miss Oliver sit upon by the minister now and then .
Susan be very fond of her but she think Miss Oliver like say heretical thing to minister far too well , and deserve an occasional reminder that these matter be quite beyond her province .
In May Walter write home that he have be award a D.C. Medal .
He do not say what for , but the other boy take care that the Glen should know the brave thing Walter have do .
`` In any war but this , '' write Jerry Meredith , `` it would have mean a V.C . .
But they ca n't make V.C . 's as common a the brave thing do every day here . ''
`` He should have have the V.C . , '' say Susan , and be very indignant over it .
She be not quite sure who be to blame for his not get it , but if it be General Haig she begin for the first time to entertain serious doubt a to his fitness for be Commander-in-Chief .
Rilla be beside herself with delight .
It be her dear Walter who have do this thing -- Walter , to whom someone have send a white feather at Redmond -- it be Walter who have dash back from the safety of the trench to drag in a wounded comrade who have fall on No-man 's - land .
Oh , she could see his white beautiful face and wonderful eye a he do it !
What a thing to be the sister of such a hero !
And he have n't think it worth while write about .
His letter be full of other thing -- little intimate thing that they two have know and love together in the dear old cloudless day of a century ago .
`` I 've be think of the daffodil in the garden at Ingleside , '' he write .
`` By the time you get this they will be out , blow there under that lovely rosy sky .
Are they really a bright and golden a ever , Rilla ?
It seem to me that they must be dye red with blood -- like our poppy here .
And every whisper of spring will be fall a a violet in Rainbow Valley .
`` There be a young moon tonight -- a slender , silver , lovely thing hanging over these pit of torment .
Will you see it tonight over the maple grove ?
`` I 'm enclose a little scrap of verse , Rilla .
I write it one evening in my trench dug-out by the light of a bit of candle -- or rather it come to me there -- I do n't feel a if I be write it -- something seem to use me a an instrument .

It print it and the copy come today .
I hope you 'll like it .

The poem be a short , poignant little thing .
In a month it have carry Walter 's name to every corner of the globe .
Everywhere it be copy -- in metropolitan daily and little village weekly -- in profound review and `` agony column , '' in Red Cross appeal and Government recruit propaganda .
Mothers and sister weep over it , young lad thrill to it , the whole great heart of humanity caught it up a an epitome of all the pain and hope and pity and purpose of the mighty conflict , crystallize in three brief immortal verse .
A Canadian lad in the Flanders trench have write the one great poem of the war .
`` The Piper , '' by Pte . .
Walter Blythe , be a classic from it first printing .
Rilla copy it in her diary at the beginning of an entry in which she pour out the story of the hard week that have just pass .
`` It have be such a dreadful week , '' she write , `` and even though it be over and we know that it be all a mistake that do not seem to do away with the bruise leave by it .
And yet it have in some way be a very wonderful week and I have have some glimpse of thing I never realize before -- of how fine and brave people can be even in the midst of horrible suffering .
I be sure I could never be as splendid a Miss Oliver be .
`` Just a week ago today she have a letter from Mr. Grant 's mother in Charlottetown .
And it tell her that a cable have just come say that Major Robert Grant have be kill in action a few day before .
`` Oh , poor Gertrude !
At first she be crush .
Then after just a day she pull herself together and go back to her school .
She do not cry -- I never saw her shed a tear -- but oh , her face and her eye ! '' '
I must go on with my work , ' she say .
` That be my duty just now . '
`` I could never have rise to such a height .
`` She never speak bitterly except once , when Susan say something about spring be here at last , and Gertrude say , '' ` Can the spring really come this year ? '
`` Then she laugh -- such a dreadful little laugh , just a one might laugh in the face of death , I think , and say , '' ` Observe my egotism .
Because I , Gertrude Oliver , have lose a friend , it be incredible that the spring can come a usual .
The spring do not fail because of the million agony of others -- but for mine -- oh , can the universe go on ? ' ''
` Do n't feel bitter with yourself , dear , ' mother say gently .
` It be a very natural thing to feel a if thing could n't go on just the same when some great blow have change the world for u .
We all feel like that . '
`` Then that horrid old Cousin Sophia of Susan 's pip up .
She be sit there , knit and croak like an old ` raven of bode and woe ' a Walter use to call her . ''
` You ai n't a bad off a some , Miss Oliver , ' she say , ` and you should n't take it so hard .
There 's some a have lose their husband ; that 's a hard blow ; and there 's some a have lose their son .
You have n't lose either husband or son . ' ''
` No , ' say Gertrude , more bitterly still .
` It 's true I have n't lose a husband -- I have only lose the man who would have be my husband .

` It be n't ladylike to talk like that , ' say Cousin Sophia in a shocked tone ; and then Gertrude laugh right out , so wildly that Cousin Sophia be really frighten .
And when poor torture Gertrude , unable to endure it any longer , hurry out of the room , Cousin Sophia ask mother if the blow have n't affect Miss Oliver 's mind . '' '
I suffer the loss of two good kind partner , ' she say , ` but it do not affect me like that . '
`` I should think it would n't !
Those poor men must have be thankful to die .
`` I hear Gertrude walk up and down her room most of the night .
She walk like that every night .
But never so long a that night .
And once I hear her give a dreadful sudden little cry a if she have be stab .
I could n't sleep for suffer with her ; and I could n't help her .
I think the night would never end .
But it do ; and then ` joy come in the morning ' a the Bible say .
Only it do n't come exactly in the morning but well along in the afternoon .

`` I hang up the telephone and fly to Rainbow Valley .
I 'm sure I do fly -- I ca n't remember my foot ever touch the ground .
I meet Gertrude on her way home from school in the glade of spruce where we use to play , and I just gasp out the news to her .
I ought to have have more sense , of course .
But I be so crazy with joy and excitement that I never stop to think .
Gertrude just drop there among the golden young fern a if she have be shoot .
The fright it give me ought to make me sensible -- in this respect at least -- for the rest of my life .
I think I have kill her -- I remember that her mother have die very suddenly from heart failure when quite a young woman .
It seem year to me before I discover that her heart be still beat .
A pretty time I have !
I never saw anybody faint before , and I know there be nobody up at the house to help , because everybody else have go to the station to meet Di and Nan come home from Redmond .
But I know -- theoretically -- how people in a faint should be treat , and now I know it practically .
Luckily the brook be handy , and after I have work frantically over her for a while Gertrude come back to life .
She never say one word about my news and I do n't dare to refer to it again .
I help her walk up through the maple grove and up to her room , and then she say , ` Rob -- be -- living , ' a if the word be tear out of her , and fling herself on her bed and cried and cried and cry .

She cry most of last night , I think , but her face this morning look a if she have see a vision of some kind , and we be all so happy that we be almost afraid .
`` Di and Nan be home for a couple of week .
Then they go back to Red Cross work in the training camp at Kingsport .

Father say I 'm do just as good work here , with Jims and my Junior Reds .

`` Kut have fall .
It be almost a relief when it do fall , we have be dread it so long .

`` Susan be an old brick , and the way she flatten out poor Cousin Sophia be beautiful to behold .
`` As for Verdun , the battle go on and on , and we see-saw between hope and fear .
