You would have think , would you not , Mrs. Dr. dear , that a hint like that would have be enough for him !
But it go no deep than his skin .
I saw him settle back quite comfortable , a if for a good talk , and think I , ` If there be anything come it may as well come soon and be do with , for with all these rag to dye before supper I have no time to waste in flirting , ' so I speak right out .
` If you have anything particular to discuss with me , Mr. Pryor , I would feel obliged if you would mention it without loss of time , because I be very busy this afternoon . '
He fairly beam at me out of that circle of red whisker , and say , ` You be a business-like woman and I agree with you .
There be no use in waste time beat around the bush .
I come up here today to ask you to marry me . '
So there it be , Mrs. Dr. dear .
I have a proposal at last , after wait sixty-four year for one .
`` I just glare at that presumptuous creature and I say , ' I would not marry you if you be the last man on earth , Josiah Pryor .
So there you have my answer and you can take it away forthwith . '
You never saw a man so take aback a he be , Mrs. Dr. dear .
He be so flabbergasted that he just blurt out the truth .
` Why , I think you 'd be only too glad to get a chance to be marry , ' he say .
That be when I lose my head , Mrs. Dr. dear .
Do you think I have a good excuse , when a Hun and a pacifist make such an insulting remark to me ?
` Go , ' I thunder , and I just catch up that iron pot .
I could see that he think I have suddenly go insane , and I suppose he consider an iron pot full of boil dye be a dangerous weapon in the hand of a lunatic .
At any rate he go , and stand not upon the order of his go , a you saw for yourself .
And I do not think we will see him back here propose to u again in a hurry .
No , I think he have learn that there be at least one single woman in Glen St. Mary who have no hankering to become Mrs. Whiskers-on-the-moon . ''
CHAPTER XXVII WAITING Ingleside , 1st November 1917 `` It be November -- and the Glen be all grey and brown , except where the Lombardy poplar stand up here and there like great golden torch in the sombre landscape , although every other tree have shed it leaf .
It have be very hard to keep our courage alight of late .
The Caporetto disaster be a dreadful thing and not even Susan can extract much consolation out of the present state of affair .
The rest of u do n't try .
Gertrude keep say desperately , ` They must not get Venice -- they must not get Venice , ' a if by say it often enough she can prevent them .
But what be to prevent them from get Venice I can not see .
Yet , a Susan fail not to point out , there be seemingly nothing to prevent them from get to Paris in 1914 , yet they do not get it , and she affirm they shall not get Venice either .
Oh , how I hope and pray they will not -- Venice the beautiful Queen of the Adriatic .
Although I 've never see it I feel about it just a Byron do -- I 've always love it -- it have always be to me ' a fairy city of the heart . '
Perhaps I catch my love of it from Walter , who worship it .
It be always one of his dream to see Venice .
I remember we plan once -- down in Rainbow Valley one evening just before the war break out -- that some time we would go together to see it and float in a gondola through it moonlit street .
`` Every fall since the war begin there have be some terrible blow to our troop -- Antwerp in 1914 , Serbia in 1915 ; last fall , Rumania , and now Italy , the bad of all .
I think I would give up in despair if it be not for what Walter say in his dear last letter -- that ` the dead as well a the living be fight on our side and such an army can not be defeat . '
No it can not .
We will win in the end .
I will not doubt it for one moment .
To let myself doubt would be to ` break faith . '
`` We have all be campaign furiously of late for the new Victory Loan .
We Junior Reds canvass diligently and land several tough old customer who have at first flatly refuse to invest .
I -- even I -- tackle Whiskers-on-the-moon .
I expect a bad time and a refusal .
But to my amazement he be quite agreeable and promise on the spot to take a thousand dollar bond .
He may be a pacifist , but he know a good investment when it be hand out to him .
Five and a half per cent be finve and a half per cent , even when a militaristic government pay it .
`` Father , to tease Susan , say it be her speech at the Victory Loan Campaign meeting that convert Mr. Pryor .
I do n't think that at all likely , since Mr. Pryor have be publicly very bitter against Susan ever since her quite unmistakable rejection of his lover-like advance .
But Susan do make a speech -- and the best one make at the meeting , too .
It be the first time she ever do such a thing and she vow it will be the last .
Everybody in the Glen be at the meeting , and quite a number of speech be make , but somehow thing be a little flat and no especial enthusiasm could be work up .
Susan be quite dismay at the lack of zeal , because she have be burningly anxious that the Island should go over the top in regard to it quota .
She keep whisper viciously to Gertrude and me that there be ` no ginger ' in the speech ; and when nobody go forward to subscribe to the loan at the close Susan ` lose her head . '
At least , that be how she describe it herself .
She bound to her foot , her face grim and set under her bonnet -- Susan be the only woman in Glen St. Mary who still wear a bonnet -- and say sarcastically and loudly , ` No doubt it be much cheap to talk patriotism than it be to pay for it .
And we be ask charity , of course -- we be ask you to lend u your money for nothing !
No doubt the Kaiser will feel quite downcast when he hear of this meeting ! ''
`` Susan have an unshaken belief that the Kaiser 's spy -- presumably represent by Mr. Pryor -- promptly inform him of every happening in our Glen .
`` Norman Douglas shout out ` Hear !
Hear ! '
and some boy at the back say , ` What about Lloyd George ? '
in a tone Susan do n't like .
Lloyd George be her pet hero , now that Kitchener be go . '' '
I stand behind Lloyd George every time , ' retort Susan . '' '
I suppose that will hearten him up greatly , ' say Warren Mead , with one of his disagreeable ` haw-haws . '
`` Warren 's remark be spark to powder .
Susan just ` sail in ' a she put it , and ` say her say . '
She say it remarkably well , too .
There be no lack of ` ginger ' in her speech , anyhow .
When Susan be warm up she have no mean power of oratory , and the way she trim those men down be funny and wonderful and effective all at once .
She say it be the like of her , million of her , that do stand behind Lloyd George , and do hearten him up .
That be the key-note of her speech .
Dear old Susan !
She be a perfect dynamo of patriotism and loyalty and contempt for slacker of all kind , and when she let it loose on that audience in her one grand outburst she electrify it .
Susan always vow she be no suffragette , but she give womanhood it due that night , and she literally make those men cringe .
When she finish with them they be ready to eat out of her hand .
She wind up by order them -- yes , order them -- to march up to the platform forthwith and subscribe for Victory Bonds .
And after wild applause most of them do it , even Warren Mead .
When the total amount subscribe come out in the Charlottetown dailies the next day we find that the Glen lead every district on the Island -- and certainly Susan have the credit for it .
She , herself , after she come home that night be quite ashamed and evidently fear that she have be guilty of unbecoming conduct : she confess to mother that she have be ` rather unladylike . '
`` We be all -- except Susan -- out for a trial ride in father 's new automobile tonight .
A very good one we have , too , though we do get ingloriously ditch at the end , owe to a certain grim old dame -- to wit , Miss Elizabeth Carr of the Upper Glen -- who would n't rein her horse out to let u pass , honk a we might .
Father be quite furious ; but in my heart I believe I sympathize with Miss Elizabeth .
If I have be a spinster lady , drive along behind my own old nag , in maiden meditation fancy free , I would n't have lift a rein when an obstreperous car hoot blatantly behind me .
I should just have sit up as dourly a she do and say ` Take the ditch if you be determine to pass . '
`` We do take the ditch -- and get up to our axle in sand -- and sat foolishly there while Miss Elizabeth cluck up her horse and rattle victoriously away .
`` Jem will have a laugh when I write him this .
He know Miss Elizabeth of old .
`` But -- will -- Venice -- be -- save ? ''
19th November 1917 `` It be not save yet -- it be still in great danger .
But the Italians be make a stand at last on the Piave line .
To be sure military critic say they can not possibly hold it and must retreat to the Adige .
But Susan and Gertrude and I say they must hold it , because Venice must be save , so what be the military critic to do ?
`` Oh , if I could only believe that they can hold it !
`` Our Canadian troop have win another great victory -- they have storm the Passchendaele Ridge and hold it in the face of all counter attack .
None of our boy be in the battle -- but oh , the casualty list of other people 's boy !
Joe Milgrave be in it but come through safe .
Miranda have some bad day until she get word from him .
But it be wonderful how Miranda have bloom out since her marriage .
She be n't the same girl at all .
Even her eye seem to have darken and deepen -- though I suppose that be just because they glow with the great intensity that have come to her .
She make her father stand round in a perfectly amazing fashion ; she run up the flag whenever a yard of trench on the western front be take ; and she come up regularly to our Junior Red Cross ; and she do -- yes , she do -- put on funny little ` married woman ' air that be quite kill .
But she be the only war-bride in the Glen and surely nobody need grudge her the satisfaction she get out of it .
`` The Russian news be bad , too -- Kerensky 's government have fall and Lenin be dictator of Russia .
Somehow , it be very hard to keep up courage in the dull hopelessness of these grey autumn day of suspense and bode news .
But we be begin to ` get in a low , ' a old Highland Sandy say , over the approaching election .
Conscription be the real issue at stake and it will be the most exciting election we ever have .
All the woman ` who have get de age ' -- to quote Jo Poirier , and who have husband , son , and brother at the front , can vote .
Oh , if I be only twenty-one !
Gertrude and Susan be both furious because they ca n't vote . ''
` It be not fair , ' Gertrude say passionately .
` There be Agnes Carr who can vote because her husband go .
She do everything she could to prevent him from go , and now she be go to vote against the Union Government .
Yet I have no vote , because my man at the front be only my sweetheart and not my husband ! ''
`` As for Susan , when she reflect that she can not vote , while a rank old pacifist like Mr. Pryor can -- and will -- her comment be sulphurous .
`` I really feel sorry for the Elliotts and Crawfords and MacAllisters over-harbour .
They have always line up in clearly divide camp of Liberal and Conservative , and now they be tear from their mooring -- I know I 'm mix my metaphor dreadfully -- and set hopelessly adrift .
It will kill some of those old Grits to vote for Sir Robert Borden 's side -- and yet they have to because they believe the time have come when we must have conscription .
And some poor Conservatives who be against conscription must vote for Laurier , who always have be anathema to them .
Some of them be take it terribly hard .
Others seem to be in much the same attitude a Mrs. Marshall Elliott have come to be regard Church Union .
`` She be up here last night .
She do n't come as often a she use to .
She be grow too old to walk this far -- dear old ` Miss Cornelia . '
I hate to think of her grow old -- we have always love her so and she have always be so good to u Ingleside young fry .
`` She use to be so bitterly oppose to Church Union .
But last night , when father tell her it be practically decide , she say in a resigned tone , ` Well , in a world where everything be be rent and torn what matter one more rending and tearing ?
Anyhow , compare with Germans even Methodists seem attractive to me . '
`` Our Junior R.C . go on quite smoothly , in spite of the fact that Irene have come back to it -- have fall out with the Lowbridge society , I understand .
She give me a sweet little jab last meeting -- about know me across the square in Charlottetown ` by my green velvet hat . '
Everybody know me by that detestable and detest hat .
This will be my fourth season for it .
Even mother want me to get a new one this fall ; but I say , ` No . '
As long a the war last so long do I wear that velvet hat in winter . ''
23rd November 1917 `` The Piave line still hold -- and General Byng have win a splendid victory at Cambrai .
I do run up the flag for that -- but Susan only say ' I shall set a kettle of water on the kitchen range tonight .
I notice little Kitchener always have an attack of croup after any British victory .
I do hope he have no pro-German blood in his vein .
Nobody know much about his father 's people . '
`` Jims have have a few attack of croup this fall -- just the ordinary croup -- not that terrible thing he have last year .
But whatever blood run in his little vein it be good , healthy blood .
He be rosy and plump and curly and cute ; and he say such funny thing and asks such comical question .
He like very much to sit in a special chair in the kitchen ; but that be Susan 's favourite chair , too , and when she want it , out Jims must go .
The last time she put him out of it he turn around and ask solemnly , ` When you be dead , Susan , can I sit in that chair ? '
Susan think it quite dreadful , and I think that be when she begin to feel anxiety about his possible ancestry .
The other night I take Jims with me for a walk down to the store .
It be the first time he have ever be out so late at night , and when he saw the star he exclaim , ` Oh , Willa , see the big moon and all the little moon ! '
And last Wednesday morning , when he wake up , my little alarm clock have stop because I have forget to wind it up .
Jims bound out of his crib and run across to me , his face quite aghast above his little blue flannel pyjama .
` The clock be dead , ' he gasp , ` oh Willa , the clock be dead . '
`` One night he be quite angry with both Susan and me because we would not give him something he want very much .
When he say his prayer he plump down wrathfully , and when he come to the petition ` Make me a good boy ' he tack on emphatically , ` and please make Willa and Susan good , 'cause they 're not . '
`` I do n't go about quote Jims 's speech to all I meet .
That always bore me when other people do it !
I just enshrine them in this old hotch-potch of a journal !
`` This very evening a I put Jims to bed he look up and ask me gravely , ` Why ca n't yesterday come back , Willa ? '
`` Oh , why ca n't it , Jims ?
That beautiful ` yesterday ' of dream and laughter -- when our boy be home -- when Walter and I read and ramble and watch new moon and sunset together in Rainbow Valley .
If it could just come back !
But yesterday never come back , little Jims -- and the today be dark with cloud -- and we dare not think about the tomorrow . ''
11th December 1917 `` Wonderful news come today .
The British troop capture Jerusalem yesterday .
We run up the flag and some of Gertrude 's old sparkle come back to her for a moment . ''
` After all , ' she say , ` it be worth while to live in the day which see the object of the Crusades attain .
The ghost of all the Crusaders must have crowd the wall of Jerusalem last night , with Coeur-de-lion at their head . '
`` Susan have cause for satisfaction also . '' '
I be so thankful I can pronounce Jerusalem and Hebron , ' she say .
` They give me a real comfortable feeling after Przemysl and Brest-Litovsk !
Well , we have get the Turks on the run , at least , and Venice be safe and Lord Lansdowne be not to be take seriously ; and I see no reason why we should be downhearted . '
`` Jerusalem !
The ` meteor flag of England ! '
float over you -- the Crescent be go .
How Walter would have thrill over that ! ''
18th December 1917 `` Yesterday the election come off .
In the evening mother and Susan and Gertrude and I forgather in the living-room and wait in breathless suspense , father have go down to the village .
We have no way of hear the news , for Carter Flagg 's store be not on our line , and when we try to get it Central always answer that the line ` be busy ' -- a no doubt it be , for everybody for mile around be try to get Carter 's store for the same reason we be .
`` About ten o'clock Gertrude go to the ` phone and happen to catch someone from over-harbour talk to Carter Flagg .
Gertrude shamelessly listen in and get for her comfort what eavesdropper be proverbially suppose to get -- to wit , unpleasant hearing ; the Union Government have ` do nothing ' in the West .
`` We look at each other in dismay .
If the Government have fail to carry the West , it be defeat . ''
` Canada be disgrace in the eye of the world , ' say Gertrude bitterly . ''
` If everybody be like the Mark Crawfords over-harbour this would not have happen , ' groan Susan .
` Yhey lock their Uncle up in the barn this morning and would not let him out until he promise to vote Union .
That be what I call effective argument , Mrs. Dr. dear . '
`` Gertrude and I could n't rest after all that .
We walk the floor until our leg give out and we have to sit down perforce .
Mother knit away as steadily a clockwork and pretend to be calm and serene -- pretend so well that we be all deceive and envious until the next day , when I catch her ravel out four inch of her sock .
She have knit that far past where the heel should have begin !
`` It be twelve before father come home .
He stand in the doorway and look at u and we look at him .
We do not dare ask him what the news be .
Then he say that it be Laurier who have ` do nothing ' in the West , and that the Union Government be in with a big majority .
Gertrude clap her hand .
I want to laugh and cry , mother 's eye flash with their old-time starriness and Susan emit a queer sound between a gasp and a whoop .
`` This will not comfort the Kaiser much , ' she say .
`` Then we go to bed , but be too excite to sleep .
Really , a Susan say solemnly this morning , ` Mrs. Dr. dear , I think politics be too strenuous for woman . ' ''
31st December 1917 `` Our fourth War Christmas be over .
We be try to gather up some courage wherewith to face another year of it .
Germany have , for the most part , be victorious all summer .
And now they say she have all her troop from the Russian front ready for a ` big push ' in the spring .
Sometimes it seem to me that we just can not live through the winter wait for that .
`` I have a great batch of letter from overseas this week .
Shirley be at the front now , too , and write about it all a coolly and matter-of-factly a he use to write of football at Queen 's .
Carl write that it have be rain for week and that night in the trench always make him think of the night of long ago when he do penance in the graveyard for run away from Henry Warren 's ghost .
Carl 's letter be always full of joke and bit of fun .
They have a great rat-hunt the night before he write -- spear rat with their bayonet -- and he get the best bag and win the prize .
He have a tame rat that know him and sleep in his pocket at night .
Rats do n't worry Carl a they do some people -- he be always chummy with all little beast .
He say he be make a study of the habit of the trench rat and mean to write a treatise on it some day that will make him famous .
`` Ken write a short letter .
His letter be all rather short now -- and he do n't often slip in those dear little sudden sentence I love so much .
Sometimes I think he have forget all about the night he be here to say goodbye -- and then there will be just a line or a word that make me think he remembers and always will remember .
For instance to-day 's letter have n't a thing in it that might n't have be write to any girl , except that he sign himself ` Your Kenneth , ' instead of ` Yours , Kenneth , ' a he usually do .
Now , do he leave that 's ' off intentionally or be it only carelessness ?
I shall lie awake half the night wondering .
He be a captain now .
I be glad and proud -- and yet Captain Ford sound so horribly far away and high up .
Ken and Captain Ford seem like two different person .
I may be practically engage to Ken -- mother 's opinion on that point be my stay and bulwark -- but I ca n't be to Captain Ford !
`` And Jem be a lieutenant now -- win his promotion on the field .
He send me a snap-shot , take in his new uniform .
He look thin and old -- old -- my boy-brother Jem .
I ca n't forget mother 's face when I show it to her .
` That -- my little Jem -- the baby of the old House of Dreams ? '
be all she say .
`` There be a letter from Faith , too .
She be do V.A.D . work in England and write hopefully and brightly .
I think she be almost happy -- she saw Jem on his last leave and she be so near him she could go to him , if he be wound .
That mean so much to her .
Oh , if I be only with her !
But my work be here at home .
I know Walter would n't have want me to leave mother and in everything I try to ` keep faith ' with him , even to the little detail of daily life .
Walter die for Canada -- I must live for her .
That be what he ask me to do . ''
28th January 1918 '' ' I shall anchor my storm-tossed soul to the British fleet and make a batch of bran biscuit , ' say Susan today to Cousin Sophia , who have come in with some weird tale of a new and all-conquering submarine , just launch by Germany .
But Susan be a somewhat disgruntled woman at present , owe to the regulation regard cookery .
Her loyalty to the Union Government be be sorely try .
It surmount the first strain gallantly .
When the order about flour come Susan say , quite cheerfully , ' I be an old dog to be learn new trick , but I shall learn to make war bread if it will help defeat the Huns . '
`` But the late suggestion go against Susan 's grain .
Had it not be for father 's decree I think she would have snap her finger at Sir Robert Borden . ''
` Talk about try to make brick without straw , Mrs. Dr. dear !
How be I to make a cake without butter or sugar ?
It can not be do -- not cake that be cake .
Of course one can make a slab , Mrs. Dr. dear .
And we can not even camooflash it with a little icing !
To think that I should have live to see the day when a government at Ottawa should step into my kitchen and put me on ration ! '
`` Susan would give the last drop of her blood for her ` king and country , ' but to surrender her beloved recipe be a very different and much more serious matter .
`` I have letter from Nan and Di too -- or rather note .
They be too busy to write letter , for exam be loom up .
They will graduate in Arts this spring .
I be evidently to be the dunce of the family .
But somehow I never have any hankering for a college course , and even now it do n't appeal to me .
I 'm afraid I 'm rather devoid of ambition .
There be only one thing I really want to be -- and I do n't know if I 'll be it or not .
If not -- I do n't want to be anything .
But I sha n't write it down .
It be all right to think it ; but , a Cousin Sophia would say , it might be brazen to write it down .
`` I will write it down .
I wo n't be cow by the convention and Cousin Sophia !
I want to be Kenneth Ford 's wife !
There now !
`` I 've just look in the glass , and I have n't the sign of a blush on my face .
I suppose I 'm not a properly construct damsel at all .
`` I be down to see little Dog Monday today .
He have grow quite stiff and rheumatic but there he sit , wait for the train .
He thump his tail and look pleadingly into my eye .
` When will Jem come ? '
he seem to say .
Oh , Dog Monday , there be no answer to that question ; and there be , a yet , no answer to the other which we be all constantly ask ` What will happen when Germany strike again on the western front -- her one great , last blow for victory ! ''
1st March 1918 '' ` What will spring bring ? '
Gertrude say today . '
I dread it a I never dread spring before .
Do you suppose there will ever again come a time when life will be free from fear ?
For almost four year we have lie down with fear and rise up with it .
It have be the unbidden guest at every meal , the unwelcome companion at every gathering . ' ''
` Hindenburg say he will be in Paris on 1st April , ' sigh Cousin Sophia . ''
` Hindenburg ! '
There be no power in pen and ink to express the contempt which Susan infuse into that name .
` Has he forget what day the first of April be ? ' ''
` Hindenburg have keep his word hitherto , ' say Gertrude , as gloomily a Cousin Sophia herself could have say it . ''
` Yes , fight against the Russians and Rumanians , ' retort Susan .
` Wait you till he come up against the British and French , not to speak of the Yankees , who be get there as fast a they can and will no doubt give a good account of themselves . ' ''
` You say just the same thing before Mons , Susan , ' I remind her . ''
` Hindenburg say he will spend a million life to break the Allied front , ' say Gertrude .
` At such a price he must purchase some success and how can we live through them , even if he be baffle in the end .
These past two month when we have be crouch and wait for the blow to fall have seem as long a all the precede month of the war put together .
I work all day feverishly and waken at three o'clock at night to wonder if the iron legion have strike at last .
It be then I see Hindenburg in Paris and Germany triumphant .
I never see her so at any other time than that accurse hour . '
`` Susan look dubious over Gertrude 's adjective , but evidently conclude that the ` a ' save the situation . '' '
I wish it be possible to take some magic draught and go to sleep for the next three month -- and then waken to find Armageddon over , ' say mother , almost impatiently .
`` It be not often that mother slump into a wish like that -- or at least the verbal expression of it .
Mother have change a great deal since that terrible day in September when we know that Walter would not come back ; but she have always be brave and patient .
Now it seem a if even she have reach the limit of her endurance .
`` Susan go over to mother and touch her shoulder . ''
` Do not you be frighten or downhearted , Mrs. Dr. dear , ' she say gently . '
I felt somewhat that way myself last night , and I rise from my bed and light my lamp and open my Bible ; and what do you think be the first verse my eye light upon ?
It be ` And they shall fight against thee but they shall not prevail against thee , for I be with thee , saith the Lord of Hosts , to deliver thee . '
I be not gift in the way of dreaming , a Miss Oliver be , but I know then and there , Mrs. Dr. dear , that it be a manifest leading , and that Hindenburg will never see Paris .
So I read no far but go back to my bed and I do not waken at three o'clock or at any other hour before morning . '
`` I say that verse Susan read over and over again to myself .
The Lord of Hosts be with u -- and the spirit of all just men make perfect -- and even the legion and gun that Germany be mass on the western front must break against such a barrier .
This be in certain uplifted moment ; but when other moment come I feel , like Gertrude , that I can not endure any longer this awful and ominous hush before the come storm . ''
23rd March 1918 `` Armageddon have begin !
-- ` the last great fight of all ! '
Is it , I wonder ?
Yesterday I go down to the post office for the mail .
It be a dull , bitter day .
The snow be go but the grey , lifeless ground be frozen hard and a biting wind be blow .
The whole Glen landscape be ugly and hopeless .
`` Then I get the paper with it big black headline .
Germany strike on the twenty-first .
She make big claim of gun and prisoner take .
General Haig report that ` severe fighting continue . '
I do n't like the sound of that last expression .
`` We all find we can not do any work that require concentration of thought .
So we all knit furiously , because we can do that mechanically .
At least the dreadful waiting be over -- the horrible wondering where and when the blow will fall .
It have fall -- but they shall not prevail against u !
`` Oh , what be happen on the western front tonight a I write this , sit here in my room with my journal before me ?
Jims be asleep in his crib and the wind be wail around the window ; over my desk hang Walter 's picture , look at me with his beautiful deep eye ; the Mona Lisa he give me the last Christmas he be home hang on one side of it , and on the other a framed copy of `` The Piper . ''
It seem to me that I can hear Walter 's voice repeat it -- that little poem into which he put his soul , and which will therefore live for ever , carry Walter 's name on through the future of our land .
Everything about me be calm and peaceful and ` homey . '
Walter seem very near me -- if I could just sweep aside the thin wavering little veil that hang between , I could see him -- just a he saw the Pied Piper the night before Courcelette .
`` Over there in France tonight -- do the line hold ? ''
CHAPTER XXVIII BLACK SUNDAY In March of the year of grace 1918 there be one week into which must have crowd more of sear human agony than any seven day have ever hold before in the history of the world .
And in that week there be one day when all humanity seem nailed to the cross ; on that day the whole planet must have be agroan with universal convulsion ; everywhere the heart of men be fail them for fear .
It dawn calmly and coldly and greyly at Ingleside .
Mrs. Blythe and Rilla and Miss Oliver make ready for church in a suspense temper by hope and confidence .
The doctor be away , have be summon during the wee sma 's to the Marwood household in Upper Glen , where a little war-bride be fight gallantly on her own battleground to give life , not death , to the world .
Susan announce that she mean to stay home that morning -- a rare decision for Susan .
`` But I would rather not go to church this morning , Mrs. Dr. dear , '' she explain .
`` If Whiskers-on-the-moon be there and I saw him look holy and pleased , a he always look when he think the Huns be win , I fear I would lose my patience and my sense of decorum and hurl a Bible or hymn-book at him , thereby disgrace myself and the sacred edifice .
No , Mrs. Dr. dear , I shall stay home from church till the tide turn and pray hard here . ''
`` I think I might as well stay home , too , for all the good church will do me today , '' Miss Oliver say to Rilla , a they walk down the hard-frozen red road to the church .
`` I can think of nothing but the question , ` Does the line still hold ? ' ''
`` Next Sunday will be Easter , '' say Rilla .
`` Will it herald death or life to our cause ? ''
Mr. Meredith preach that morning from the text , `` He that endureth to the end shall be save , '' and hope and confidence rang through his inspiring sentence .
Rilla , look up at the memorial tablet on the wall above their pew , `` sacred to the memory of Walter Cuthbert Blythe , '' felt herself lift out of her dread and fill anew with courage .
Walter could not have lay down his life for naught .
His have be the gift of prophetic vision and he have foreseen victory .
She would cling to that belief -- the line would hold .
In this renew mood she walk home from church almost gaily .
The others , too , be hopeful , and all go smile into Ingleside .
There be no one in the living-room , save Jims , who have fall asleep on the sofa , and Doc , who sit `` hush in grim repose '' on the hearth-rug , look very Hydeish indeed .
No one be in the dining-room either -- and , strange still , no dinner be on the table , which be not even set .
Where be Susan ?
`` Can she have take ill ? ''
exclaim Mrs. Blythe anxiously .
`` I think it strange that she do not want to go to church this morning . ''
The kitchen door open and Susan appear on the threshold with such a ghastly face that Mrs. Blythe cry out in sudden panic .
`` Susan , what be it ? ''
`` The British line be break and the German shell be fall on Paris , '' say Susan dully .
The three woman star at each other , stricken .
`` It 's not true -- it 's not , '' gasp Rilla .
`` The thing would be -- ridiculous , '' say Gertrude Oliver -- and then she laugh horribly .
`` Susan , who tell you this -- when do the news come ? ''
ask Mrs. Blythe .
`` I get it over the long-distance phone from Charlottetown half an hour ago , '' say Susan .
`` The news come to town late last night .
It be Dr. Holland phone it out and he say it be only too true .
Since then I have do nothing , Mrs. Dr. dear .
I be very sorry dinner be not ready .
It be the first time I have be so remiss .
If you will be patient I will soon have something for you to eat .
But I be afraid I let the potato burn . ''
`` Dinner !
Nobody want any dinner , Susan , '' say Mrs. Blythe wildly .
`` Oh , this thing be unbelievable -- it must be a nightmare . ''
`` Paris be lose -- France be lose -- the war be lose , '' gasp Rilla , amid the utter ruin of hope and confidence and belief .
`` Oh God -- Oh God , '' moan Gertrude Oliver , walk about the room and wring her hand , `` Oh -- God ! ''
Nothing else -- no other word -- nothing but that age old plea -- the old , old cry of supreme agony and appeal , from the human heart whose every human staff have fail it .
`` Is God dead ? ''
ask a startled little voice from the doorway of the living-room .
Jims stood there , flush from sleep , his big brown eye fill with dread , `` Oh Willa -- oh , Willa , be God dead ? ''
Miss Oliver stop walk and exclaim , and star at Jims , in whose eye tear of fright be begin to gather .
Rilla run to his comforting , while Susan bound up from the chair upon which she have drop .
`` No , '' she say briskly , with a sudden return of her real self .
`` No , God be n't dead -- nor Lloyd George either .
We be forget that , Mrs. Dr. dear .
Do n't cry , little Kitchener .
Bad a thing be , they might be bad .
The British line may be break but the British navy be not .
Let u tie to that .
I will take a brace and get up a bite to eat , for strength we must have . ''
They make a pretence of eat Susan 's `` bite , '' but it be only a pretence .
Nobody at Ingleside ever forget that black afternoon .
Gertrude Oliver walk the floor -- they all walk the floor ; except Susan , who get out her grey war sock .
`` Mrs. Dr. dear , I must knit on Sunday at last .
I have never dream of do it before for , say what might be say , I have consider it be a violation of the third commandment .
But whether it be or whether it be not I must knit today or I shall go mad . ''
`` Knit if you can , Susan , '' say Mrs. Blythe restlessly .
`` I would knit if I could -- but I can not -- I can not . ''
`` If we could only get full information , '' moan Rilla .
`` There might be something to encourage u -- if we know all . ''
`` We know that the Germans be shell Paris , '' say Miss Oliver bitterly .
`` In that case they must have smash through everywhere and be at the very gate .
No , we have lose -- let u face the fact a other people in the past have have to face it .
Other nation , with right on their side , have give their best and brave -- and go down to defeat in spite of it .
Ours be ` but one more To baffle million who have go before . ' ''
`` I wo n't give up like that , '' cry Rilla , her pale face suddenly flush .
`` I wo n't despair .
We be not conquer -- no , if Germany overrun all France we be not conquer .
I be ashamed of myself for this hour of despair .
You wo n't see me slump again like that , I 'm go to ring up town at once and ask for particular . ''
But town could not be get .
The long-distance operator there be submerge by similar call from every part of the distracted country .
Rilla finally give up and slip away to Rainbow Valley .
There she kneel down on the withered grey grass in the little nook where she and Walter have have their last talk together , with her head bow against the mossy trunk of a fall tree .
The sun have break through the black cloud and drench the valley with a pale golden splendour .
The bell on the Tree Lovers twinkle elfinly and fitfully in the gusty March wind .
`` Oh God , give me strength , '' Rilla whisper .
`` Just strength -- and courage . ''
Then like a child she clasp her hand together and say , as simply a Jims could have do , `` Please send u good news tomorrow . ''
She kneel there a long time , and when she go back to Ingleside she be calm and resolute .
The doctor have arrive home , tire but triumphant , little Douglas Haig Marwood have make a safe landing on the shore of time .
Gertrude be still pace restlessly but Mrs. Blythe and Susan have react from the shock , and Susan be already plan a new line of defence for the channel port .
`` As long a we can hold them , '' she declare , `` the situation be save .
Paris have really no military significance . ''
`` Do n't , '' say Gertrude sharply , a if Susan have run something into her .
She think the old worn phrase ` no military significance ' nothing short of ghastly mockery under the circumstance , and more terrible to endure than the voice of despair would have be .
`` I hear up at Marwood 's of the line be break , '' say the doctor , `` but this story of the Germans shell Paris seem to be rather incredible .
Even if they break through they be fifty mile from Paris at the near point and how could they get their artillery close enough to shell it in so short a time ?
Depend upon it , girl , that part of the message ca n't be true .
I 'm go to try to try a long-distance call to town myself . ''
The doctor be no more successful than Rilla have be , but his point of view cheer them all a little , and help them through the evening .
And at nine o'clock a long-distance message come through at last , that help them through the night .
`` The line break only in one place , before St. Quentin , '' say the doctor , a he hang up the receiver , `` and the British troop be retreat in good order .
That 's not so bad .
As for the shell that be fall on Paris , they be come from a distance of seventy mile -- from some amazing long-range gun the Germans have invent and spring with the opening offensive .
That be all the news to date , and Dr. Holland say it be reliable . ''
`` It would have be dreadful news yesterday , '' say Gertrude , `` but compare to what we hear this morning it be almost like good news .
But still , '' she add , try to smile , `` I be afraid I will not sleep much tonight . ''
`` There be one thing to be thankful for at any rate , Miss Oliver , dear , '' say Susan , `` and that be that Cousin Sophia do not come in today .
I really could not have endure her on top of all the rest . ''
CHAPTER XXIX `` WOUNDED AND MISSING '' `` Battered but Not Broken '' be the headline in Monday 's paper , and Susan repeat it over and over to herself a she go about her work .
The gap cause by the St. Quentin disaster have be patch up in time , but the Allied line be be push relentlessly back from the territory they have purchase in 1917 with half a million life .
On Wednesday the headline be `` British and French Check Germans '' ; but still the retreat go on .
Back -- and back -- and back !
Where would it end ?
Would the line break again -- this time disastrously ?
